Gold and Silver 101

London Gold Price: Today (30th), the gold price rose slightly, increasing by 10.5 pence, reaching 140 shillings and 3 pence.

London Silver Bar: Today in the silver market, buying by the United States, India, and speculators caused both spot and futures prices to rise by 1.25. When the market stabilized, at a price of 21.6875 pence, China sold.

Bombay Silver Bar: Today the silver market is stable. The spot price is 59 rupees and 15 annas, September futures are 60 rupees, and October futures are 60 rupees and 2 annas, all up by 5 annas.

Exchange Rates 102

British-American: In the London foreign exchange market, there was some closing this morning, and the US dollar was stable. However, there were not many transactions afterward. The closing price for British-American exchange was 5.02125 dollars, lower than yesterday's closing price of American-British exchange by 375, with fluctuations after the turn.

The exchange rate rose 75 at 11 o'clock, fell 5625 shortly after, and then fell 75 again. At 2 p.m., it rebounded by 4375, reaching 5.03 dollars. Also, one US dollar equals 3 shillings and 11.714 pence in British currency. British-French: The opening price was 75 francs and 18, lower by 10 pounds. Fluctuations in the afternoon were very uneven. It rose 16 pounds at 11 o'clock, reaching 75 francs and 34, but at 1 p.m., it fell by 31 pounds, reaching 75 francs and 03. At 2 p.m., it rebounded by 18 pounds, with the price at 75 francs and 21.

American-British: The New York foreign exchange market was quiet this morning. The British pound did not fall further. The opening price for American-British exchange was 5.05 dollars, down by half a cent, but it immediately rose by 25, reaching 5.0325 dollars. This price remained unchanged at 10:40 a.m.

Cotton and Wheat 103

New York Cotton: Today (30th), the cotton market opened lower by 7 pounds, likely due to labor strikes in the textile industry causing unrest. The market situation in the morning was quiet and stable, with no changes in the opening prices.

Bombay Cotton: Today, the cotton market saw a rise of 1.5 rupees in the price of white cotton for the April-May period due to buying by speculators, reaching 225 rupees.

Liverpool Cotton: The cotton market lacked activity. At 1 p.m., the price for October futures was 6.93, up by 1 pound from yesterday's closing.

New York Wheat: The wheat market opened lower by 375, with a continuing downward trend in the morning.

Rubber 104

London: Today the market situation was firm. At noon, the trading price for October and December futures was 7.6875 pence, up by 0.0625 from yesterday's closing.

New York: Today the market opened higher by 15 pounds due to the firm situation in the London market, and then rose by another 3 pounds, after which it stabilized.

Unfavorable news for the market situation included: (1) Securities operators failed to attract larger transactions, leading to disappointed sellers; (2) Widespread belief that textile labor strikes were unavoidable; (3) General commerce still showed signs of decline. This morning, the securities market opened softly, with most securities showing slight declines. Talk of expansion temporarily subsided. Hangzhou Rice Prices Suddenly Surge Again 107

(Hangzhou) Amidst reports of rice prices falling in Beijing, Shanghai, and other places, Hangzhou rice prices suddenly surged by 80 cents starting from the 30th. Grade 1 rice is now 12.80 yuan per stone. The originally designated "People's Rice," which was not supposed to increase in price, has now increased by 40 cents. The municipal government convened representatives from various agencies on the morning of the 30th to discuss organizing price stabilization sales. According to Mayor Zhou Xiangxian speaking to a reporter from the Central News Agency, the provincial government has decided to purchase grain from the relatively abundant Wen-Tai prefectures to adjust the situation in the severely affected counties. Hangzhou has been ordered to start price stabilization sales first. Furthermore, the municipal government has decided to raise funds to purchase 500,000 dan of food rice to establish five major granaries for price stabilization sales. (Central News Agency dispatch, 30th)

District Public Offices in Zhejiang Province 108

To be abolished next January

(Hangzhou) Zhejiang Province is reforming its autonomy and implementing a two-level system. Municipal and county councils are required to prepare for establishment by the end of this year. All district public offices will be abolished from January 1st next year to save administrative expenses. (Central News Agency dispatch, 30th)

Zhejiang borrows one million to disburse political expenses

(Hangzhou) The Finance Department is currently borrowing one million from silver firms and banks to disburse political expenses, reportedly using the province's foil tax as collateral. The contract is expected to be signed within days. (Central News Agency dispatch, 30th)

Under Difficult and Precarious Circumstances 109

Camel Owners from Sui Province Flee Xinjiang

Guihua: Recently, dozens of camel owners have fled back from Xinjiang in a desperate state. According to them, since Jin Shuren took office, soldiers and bandits have been rampant throughout Xinjiang. Over the past few years, it is estimated that over 5,000 camels going from Sui were either seized for forced labor or robbed by bandits, resulting in complete losses. At present, prices for all goods are high, and starvation is everywhere. Placed in difficult and precarious circumstances,

we seized an opportunity in May to escape Xinjiang. Some of us pooled money to buy a skinny camel to take turns riding, while others begged along the way and walked. Only recently did we safely arrive in Sui. When we left, we were all camel owners with hundreds of camels, but now we are completely destitute. It is truly tragic. As for the obstacles from Outer Mongolia, the camel industry in Sui relies solely on the Xinjiang route. Now that it is in such a state, we earnestly hope that the authorities will pay attention and find ways to provide relief. (Central News Agency dispatch, 29th)

Qing Province Remits Aircraft Donation Funds 110

Xining: Due to the bankruptcy of rural villages and the destitution of the people in this province, only 8,100 yuan in aircraft donation funds were raised in this province. Furthermore, the realization of banknotes in silver dollars has been quite difficult. It has recently been learned that the association has specially entrusted the provincial chamber of commerce to be responsible for introducing reliable firms. The funds were remitted to the Tianjin Central Bank in two installments as deposit for the Qinghai Province aircraft donation funds. The current amount of silver dollars is 6,300, with an exchange fee of 300 yuan per thousand yuan, totaling 8,190 yuan. The funds have been transferred to the Shanghai Central Bank to be directly remitted to the National Aviation Construction Association and a receipt has been obtained from the Shanghai Central Bank. (Central News Agency dispatch, 29th)

Hailstorm Disaster in Xining County 111

Xining: In Xining County's Xiaonanchuan, Shangxiatang, and Longtai areas, dark clouds gathered at 4 p.m. on the 16th, and a large hailstorm fell, with hailstones as large as eggs. In an instant, the summer and autumn crops were completely destroyed, with no hope of harvest. The village leaders Ma Duo Yi and others have specifically petitioned the provincial government to send personnel to investigate and provide relief. (Central News Agency dispatch, 29th)

Public Telegram 112

Xiaofeng County, Zhejiang Province, Appeals for Relief: Respectfully addressed to Shen Bao, natural disasters are rampant, and drought demons are wreaking havoc. From summer to autumn, it has not rained for months. Xiaofeng, a mountainous county, has rice paddies located between ridges and mountain gullies. It is estimated that out of the tens of thousands of mu in the entire county, only a small percentage of paddy fields along the streams have timely irrigation and can be expected to have an autumn harvest. The majority of the nourishment for the main grains and miscellaneous cereals has always relied on rainwater as the source. Now, the soil is cracked, and all seedlings have withered. The farmers' stored grain has been exhausted, and no new grain is harvested. We have heard daily reports of people holding rice stalks and weeping, with entire families awaiting death. In the northern districts, the villages of Minle, Jingfeng, Zhangwu, Xishan, Yong'an, Dashou, Shangshu, Donglan, Meijia, Shangwu, Jintai, and Guihua are particularly severely affected, with extremely impoverished conditions. Tens of thousands of poor people have no rice grains, cooking fires are extinguished, and well-fields are deserted. Cries and lamentations echo everywhere, and the tragic situation is beyond words. The extent of the disaster area this year is rare in a century. Although the government is anxious above and the gentry and people are running about below, the treasury is empty and grain stores are lacking. Relief and price stabilization efforts cannot find a solution. Driven by hunger, a crisis is imminent. Apart from sending telegrams to appeal for relief, we are compelled to send this urgent telegram, earnestly requesting your esteemed newspaper to be concerned about the plight of the deeply affected people, to advocate and appeal on their behalf. If assistance with grain and congee is generously granted, the kindness will be as great as providing flesh and bones and the grace of rebirth, bestowed by your esteemed newspaper. With great urgency, we remain, the Agricultural Association, Education Association, and Women's Association of Xiaofeng County, Zhejiang Province, bowing in respect.

The Austrian Coup and the European Situation (German Correspondence) 113

The Impact of Dollfuss' Assassination

Germany's Attempt to Merge is Difficult to Realize

Austria is a massive political and economic cancer in Europe. Given the current situation, there is absolutely no way to cure it. Because the pre-war Austria was the Austro-Hungarian Empire, although it treated Germany as an elder brother, it still possessed a population of over 51 million and an area of 677,000 square kilometers. It was still a major power in Central Europe. Although its industry was relatively backward, it could still maintain its independence among the great powers. After the Treaty of Saint-Germain was established, its population was only over 6 million, and its land area was reduced to 82,400 square kilometers. Vienna alone accounts for 30% of the total population. There is absolutely no way for it to be self-sufficient in production. Especially since the world economic panic hit Europe, Austria's national economy has been drifting in the wind and rain, relying entirely on borrowing to survive. The League of Nations guaranteed a loan of 650 million gold kronen in 1921. When the Credit Anstalt Bank collapsed in 1929, it fell into another economic tragedy, and it will not be easy to find a solution in the future, or even no solution at all. Politically, merging with Germany is impossible due to the opposition of the people in the country and the opposition of the countries in the Versailles system and Italy. If it completely follows Italy's request and advances aggressively on the path of independence, it will also encounter the hidden reefs of the National Socialist Party's potential power, making it extremely difficult to succeed.

The political party that Dollfuss relied on was the Christian Social Party, the most right-wing party in Austria. Although Dollfuss, in his capacity as Prime Minister, also served as the Minister of Foreign Affairs, Public Security, Agriculture and Forestry, and National Defense, showing a very condescending and dictatorial demeanor, four of the remaining seven cabinet members were members of the Heimwehr, and their opinions were not entirely consistent with Dollfuss'. There are two facts to prove this. The first is that Deputy Prime Minister Starhemberg (leader of the Heimwehr) said, after Mussolini and Hitler met in June of this year, when Austria strongly advocated against terrorism, "It is not enough to delegate terrorist methods solely to state executives." Dollfuss, in a speech in the suburbs of Vienna, also said, "......When the country is in a time of trouble, all groups should unite and pull those who engage in terrorist acts into their own camp. When this opportunity is urgent, there must be no middle ground. Those who are not our comrades are our enemies." The opposition between the two was already very obvious. The second is that until the very last moment, on July 25th, Dollfuss was besieged by National Socialists in a room and was about to be killed, while the Minister of Security and the National Security Supervisor, Fesciak, who was also detained, was spared. This shows that Dollfuss himself did not have a firm grasp of power, and it also proves that the Heimwehr's steps were not in line with his.

The source of the Heimwehr was that after the European War, Austria was defeated, and Italian and Yugoslav troops entered Austrian territory. These troops mostly lacked control, and their actions as victorious countries led to acts of invasion and plunder everywhere. The Austrian people were eager to resist and used actual force to stop these atrocities. Therefore, rural youths and soldiers out of service automatically organized themselves in various places. Later, it developed from local to national, so it also has another name called "Vanguard Corps." This uprising, after Dollfuss was killed, Austria almost fell into an irrecoverable state of chaos. It was Starhemberg, the leader of the "Heimwehr," who led the group to suppress the National Socialist youth groups and tried to restore general order.

After Dollfuss was killed, it caused even more unrest throughout Europe. If Germany really had the intention to challenge, then it would have seized the opportunity to merge with Austria, which would have been virtually impossible. Because among the members of the "Heimwehr," there are quite a few who fully sympathize with the National Socialist Party and support the merger of Austria and Germany. However, Italy directly supports Austria's independence. If Hitler were to act rashly, he would inevitably clash with Italy first. At the same time, France, Czechoslovakia, and other related European countries clearly advocated Austria's independence. If Germany were to rise up to challenge, it would have no support, no powerful ally. Therefore, after the problem occurred, Germany did not dare to reach out again and had to let it change naturally. However, Austria is a new powder keg of European turmoil, with the potential to cause a major disaster at any time. The current calm is the effect of an artificial tranquilizer, a temporary respite. (July 31st, Berlin)

This Year's September 18th Incident 114

Japan Sends Fleet and Air Force to "Manchukuo" for Demonstration

General Suetsugu Commands Two Fleets

Rear Admiral Wada Commands Air Force

First Arriving at Dalian, Then Proceeding to Changchun and Harbin

Changchun Correspondence: Japanese Admiral Suetsugu Nobumasa, commanding the First and Second Combined Fleets, accompanied by Rear Admiral Wada, commander of the First Air Battle Squadron, with the aircraft carriers Akagi and Ryūjō, all aircraft, and the aircraft on the battleships, totaling 80 new-style aircraft, have been ordered to enter the port of Dalian on September 18th, and then all the aircraft will fly to Changchun to participate in the flight. It is known that Japan's dispatch of the Combined Fleet and a large part of the air force to the Northeast, judging from the scheduled date of entry into the port, is intended to flaunt its power, intimidate our compatriots in the Northeast, and, due to the interruption of negotiations on the East China Railway, with the situation in the Far East becoming tense, to show a threat to the Soviet Union. It is deeply regrettable that the Japanese have taken this action as the anniversary of the national crisis approaches. The actions of the fleet after arriving in Dalian and its planned activities are recorded as follows: 1. On the 17th, the Japanese fleet passed through the Pu-Changshan Islands, and at noon on the 18th, it entered Dalian. From the 19th to the 23rd, it will be anchored in the port of Dalian. On the 17th, 40 seaplanes will visit Andong in formation. On the 21st and 24th, flights will be made between Dalian and Harbin. Also, from the 20th to the 24th, 40 aircraft on the ships will visit "Manchukuo" in formation. 2. When the Japanese fleet is anchored in Dalian, officials and civilians will be allowed to visit. The fleet will allow 800 soldiers and above to inspect "Manchukuo."

3. On the 24th, the Second Fleet will leave Dalian. On the 25th, the First Fleet will leave Dalian for Lushun. At this time, student groups from "Manchukuo" and the Kwantung Leased Territory will be allowed to board the ship to observe the fleet's operations. 4. Both fleets will be anchored in Lushun on the 26th, and will leave Lushun for Qingdao on the 27th. While in Lushun, banquets will be held on the Kongō battleship on the 25th and 27th to entertain officials and civilians from "Manchukuo" and the Kwantung Leased Territory. Furthermore, Commander Suetsugu, Commander Takahashi of the Second Fleet, Commander Wada of the Air Battle Squadron, and about 30 others are scheduled to meet with officials and civilians in Dalian on September 18th, visit Changchun on the 19th, pay respects to the puppet on the 20th, give superficial performances, and interact with officials and civilians in Changchun, Harbin, and "Fengtian." They will return to Dalian on the 24th. (Northeast News Agency)

Wuyuan Disturbed by Bandits 115

丨Various Circles Eagerly Hope for Troops to Suppress Them丨

Wuyuan Correspondence: On the 22nd of this month, bandits who had fled from the Zhejiang border to the Huangjian area of Huizhou Prefecture were defeated by local militia and retreated to the Zhejiang border. They then entered Maohuang via Qingshan Niuling and re-entered Xitou in eastern Wuyuan on the 26th, engaging in widespread disturbances. Afterwards, they fled to Jiangkengkou and Yangtian in northern Wuyuan, where they established a stronghold with about 400 bandits. More than half of the branches were looted, and upon arrival, they engaged in large-scale plunder. Upon hearing the alarm, villagers, supporting the old and carrying the young, fled in droves, leaving behind empty homes. More than ten people were kidnapped, and it is reported that many have suffered. Neighboring villages have also been disturbed. The entire county is in a state of panic. Moreover, the county has suffered a drought this summer, the worst in a century, and now it is suffering from this unprecedented massive robbery, which is truly tragic. People from all walks of life eagerly hope that the local authorities will immediately dispatch troops to suppress the bandits and save the survivors.

Fujian and Jiangxi 116

Three Routes Encircle Bandit Areas

It Will Not Be Difficult to Eliminate the Remaining Bandit Areas

Xiamen Correspondence: Since the remnants of bandits along the Min River were eliminated and the bandits fleeing eastern Fujian collapsed, the anti-bandit military operations at the front have become more active. Commander-in-chief of the northern route, Gu Zhutong, has led his troops to attack Shicheng fiercely. Fierce battles have been fought for days. The Donglu Army Division of northern Fujian has also advanced towards Ninghua from Baishui in Jianning. In the Battle of Guanqiao, 1,400 to 1,500 bandits were killed. The bandits fled south, and the watchtowers along the mountains were burned down. The 1st, 5th, and 9th Army Corps of bandits in the Daxiaotao area at the junction of Liancheng, Ningyang, and Yong'an were also defeated by the Minxi Division on the 22nd, with over a thousand bandits killed. The front line of the current column is only forty miles away from Changting. The two columns of the Nanlu Army have also been reorganized and advanced into western Fujian and eastern Jiangxi. A large-scale operation on three routes has been consolidated, and it will not be difficult to eliminate the remaining bandit areas in southern Jiangxi in a unified manner. (28th)

Southern Route Army 117

Occupies Lion Fortress

The Stubborn Resistance of the Remnant Bandits Ended in a Miserable Defeat and Fled Huichang

Nanchang Correspondence: Yu Hanmou, commander of the First Column of the Southern Route Army, reported in a telegram on the 24th that he had sent troops to besiege Lion Fortress on the morning of the 22nd. The fortress has solid fortifications and is a key location in Xinfeng and Huichang. The bandits resisted stubbornly. After a fierce battle lasting three hours from dawn to noon, they were finally repelled, and the remnant bandits fled to Huichang, he said. Furthermore, the Garrison Headquarters, based on the confession of Xiong Chinong, a pseudo-staff member who surrendered, as submitted by Yu Hanmou, is quite detailed regarding the current situation in the bandit areas. The confession is excerpted as follows: The most painful thing for the people in the bandit areas at present is that there is no salt to buy, so they have to eat bland food or boil saltpeter to eat. The second is that there is no cloth to buy, and their clothes are torn and cannot cover their bodies. There is no medicine to buy when they are sick, and many die. At the same time, the bandit army forcibly conscripts strong men to serve as bandits and forces each person to pay three sheng of food to supply the bandit army with grain and forcibly purchase public bonds, forcibly recruit transport teams, etc. All of this causes the people in the bandit areas to groan in pain. Any slight resistance will be met with annihilation. Taking Gaopai Village as an example, in just thirteen or fourteen days, about a hundred civilians were slaughtered. All the people under the threat of the bandit army hope that the National Army will go to suppress the bandits so that they can have the opportunity to escape the bandit areas. (The rest omitted)

Remnants of Bandits in Southern Shandong Annihilated 118

Battle of Yitadun Was Very Intense

Jinan Correspondence: This spring, the fierce bandit Liu Guitang disturbed Shandong, repeatedly entering and leaving the Shandong border. The counties in southern Shandong were devastated by him. Although he was eventually completely exterminated, many stragglers and remnants of his troops still lurked among the people. Recently, with the rise of the green gauze curtains, they were thinking of making trouble again. Guo Hongru, Chief of Staff of the 66th Brigade of the 22nd Division stationed in Linyi, was ordered to lead troops to suppress them. On the 22nd, they first arrived at Hancun. The bandits under Xu Shangqian fled upon hearing the news. Afterwards, they encountered the bandit Yang Tingyi at Yitadun (Linyi), with about forty or fifty bandits. After fighting for two hours, except for Yang and twenty of the bandits fleeing southeast, the remaining twenty or so were unable to break through and stubbornly resisted in the three-story fort in the village. On the evening of the 24th, during heavy rain, the bandits fled out, trying to escape through the river, but were shot by ambushing machine guns, and the remnant bandits were almost completely killed. During the fierce battle, the officers and soldiers fought bravely, and some were injured. Company officer Zeng Guangrui and soldiers were injured but did not retreat, eventually annihilating the remnant bandits. Guo Hongru led his troops back to Jianyi on the 25th and reported the battle situation to Commander-in-Chief Han Fuju by telegram. Han immediately replied with praise and made arrangements to properly comfort the casualties. Wounded officers were rewarded with fifty yuan in silver, and those who did not retreat were promoted and recorded. Each wounded soldier was rewarded with twenty yuan in silver and was also promoted and recorded. (29th)

Incident of a Train Derailing in Shenyang 119

The Location Was Near Huangguantun

Passengers Were Extremely Panicked After the Accident

Beiping Correspondence: According to transportation circles, the second passenger train from Beiping to Shenyang derailed on the morning of the 24th. The train had a total of ten cars. At eleven o'clock, it was near the Sima Sanjiazi area west of Huangguantun Station when the roadbed's stone ballast was washed away by rainwater, causing the roadbed to collapse. As the train passed this area, the locomotive and the front six passenger cars derailed, almost overturning. The axle of the tenth third-class passenger car was broken, and the locomotive was also damaged. Several passengers were sitting in the first-class dining car, and it was lunchtime, so the cups and plates all fell to the ground. The Japanese train guards dispatched by the South Manchuria Railway injured their wrists. After the train accident, a locomotive and crane were urgently dispatched from Huangguantun Station to lift the cars out. The damaged tracks were repaired by workers dispatched by the railway bureau. Two third-class cars of the train could not run and were sent back to Shenyang for repairs. The original train continued west at 1:00 p.m. on the 24th and arrived at Shanhaiguan, delayed by two hours. It made up half an hour on the section inside the pass and should have arrived at Qianmen East Station at 9:18 a.m. on the 25th but only arrived at 10:48 a.m. According to passengers on the train, the situation was very panicked when the train suddenly derailed. Some people said that bandits had dug up the railroad tracks. After the train stopped, many passengers took refuge under the train. After the conductor explained that the train had derailed, the truth became clear and they came out to see what happened. This terrifying comedy came to an end. Japanese troops stationed at Huangguantun Station arrived at the accident site by electric railcar and set up guard posts. Because the green gauze curtains have recently risen and bandits are actively operating along the mountain roads, the situation in various places is extremely unstable. (26th)

Songjiang 120

Since summer, this county has experienced autumn-like weather with extreme drought. The river water has dried up, and the rural farmlands rely on the rising tides day and night. People exert all their strength to bail water, becoming exhausted and falling ill, which is often heard of. Even the farm cattle cannot withstand the labor and are not given time to rest. However, once exposed to the scorching sun, the fields become parched. Farmers eagerly await rain, especially as the rice is setting ears and urgently needs rain to regulate. Otherwise, a crop failure is feared. Fortunately, from yesterday, the scorching sun gradually subsided, and the weather became slightly cooler. Until 5:30 PM today, dark clouds gathered, thunder rumbled, and a heavy rain finally fell for about fifteen minutes before stopping. If it can continue to rain, this year's harvest can still be unaffected.

Fire During the Day Claims Two Lives

In the home of Cheng Yiyun, the head of Dongting Town in the Second District, there lived a widowed Ms. Shao Yuan, who was over forty years old and suffered from severe hearing loss. She had two daughters, one of whom was already married, and two sons. The eldest son, A'da, was a guest in another town and did not return home often. The younger son, A'er, was twenty-two years old and worked in a nearby cloth factory. Recently, he had been ill and recuperating at home. At around nine o'clock yesterday morning, A'er was still lying sick in bed, with a kerosene lamp placed on the table to boil medicine. Unexpectedly, it suddenly overturned, causing a fire. A'er woke up in a daze, but the fire was already raging and he could not escape, leading to his death in the flames. At that time, Ms. Shao Yuan had gone to the street to shop. Upon hearing the alarm, she rushed back to try to save A'er, but the fire was too fierce. Not only could she not save A'er, but her entire body was severely burned. She immediately jumped into the river, but the pain only intensified. She was later pulled out by others, but due to her severe injuries, she was in critical condition and unlikely to survive.

Merchant Corps Reorganized into Security Team

The Wuxi District Special Commissioner's Office of the Jiangsu Provincial Security Department recently received a letter from the First Section of the Provincial Security Department stating that the merchant corps in various counties, whether they employed security guards or were volunteer security guards, should be abolished and reorganized into security teams. The reorganization method should be studied by the security team and the respective county magistrates. After receiving the order, Commissioner Bai Zhujun convened a meeting of the eight county magistrates at the Training Office in the Hidden Courtyard of Chong'an Temple in Wuxi yesterday to discuss the reorganization plan. Except for Taicang, Kunshan, and Jiangyin, which did not send representatives to attend the meeting in Wuxi due to the lack of merchant corps organizations, the remaining five counties of Wuxi, Wu County, Wujin, Jiangyin, and Changshu, all had merchant corps organizations and sent representatives to attend. After discussion, it was decided that the merchant corps in the counties of Wuxi District that employ security guards would naturally be reorganized into security teams, and all volunteer security guards would be abolished. The training, command, and unified collection and expenditure of funds would be the responsibility of the county security general brigade, and the matter would be reported to the Provincial Security Department for approval.

Shanghai Chamber of Commerce Sends Telegram to the Ministry of Foreign Affairs 140

Urging the Conclusion of the Sino-Persian Commercial Treaty

Maintaining a Corner of the Chinese Tea Market

Yesterday, the Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce telegraphed the Ministry of Foreign Affairs in Nanjing, stating: "To the esteemed Ministry of Foreign Affairs, we received a letter from the Foreign Merchants Tea Trade Association this month, stating that Mr. Li Rixi, the Chinese manager of Niu Mazi Foreign Firm, recently wrote that your association's letter of July 2nd, which was forwarded to the Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce, recorded the Ministry of Foreign Affairs' telegram, stating that the Sino-Persian Commercial Treaty is under negotiation by both parties. Special attention should be paid to the issue of exporting national tea to Persia in the treaty, in order to safeguard rights and interests. The time has been long, but we have not yet seen our Ministry of Foreign Affairs sign a treaty with Persia. The annual export of national tea to Persia is very large, and Persia is indeed a foreign market for national tea. If a commercial treaty is not concluded, the national tea will be restricted by the treatment of countries without treaties, which will be difficult to develop. Furthermore, a large amount of national tea has recently been transported to Persia, but the commercial treaty has not been concluded, so the national tea remains lifeless. Therefore, we earnestly request your association to forward this to the Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce, requesting the Ministry of Foreign Affairs to conclude a treaty with Persia as soon as possible." Our chamber is concerned about the delay and believes that exchanging documents should be easy, but the Ministry of Foreign Affairs said that negotiations have reached a considerable stage and that it is unnecessary to exchange documents. We should request your association to use this case to request the Ministry of Foreign Affairs to handle it quickly, etc. It has been found that the sales of Chinese tea have long been captured by India, Ceylon, and Java. Even the Russians, who are known for selling Chinese tea, have not made significant progress since the restoration of relations, because the country has adopted a state trading system, reducing unnecessary consumption as much as possible, while also promoting tea production domestically, so it has been difficult to make progress. At this time of extreme difficulty, the sales in the corner of Persia must be maintained. In countries that adopt a multiple tax system for tariffs, the tax levied on countries without treaties is necessarily heavier than that levied on countries with treaties. Therefore, before the Sino-Persian Commercial Treaty is signed, there is no hope of reducing the tax on Chinese tea exported to Persia. Commercial treaties between the two countries have complex clauses and involve many issues, which may not be completed in a short time. Persia has signed goodwill treaties for more than ten

years, but a commercial treaty has not yet been concluded, which is a clear sign. Because our country's tariffs are based on a single tax system, with or without a treaty, the treatment is the same, they do not feel the need for a commercial treaty. In case of obstacles, or the negotiations are stopped and started, or the signing is delayed, then the sales of Chinese tea will follow the same path as the new Sino-French Vietnam treaty. We hereby re-telegraph, earnestly requesting your ministry to review, graciously grant quick handling, which is for the public good. Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce, Qian."

Ministry of Communications Building 141

Nine-Province Telephone Trunk Line

Postal Savings Bureau Invests 800,000 Yuan

Contract Drafted, Signing Soon

According to the Shen Shi News Agency, in order to facilitate direct telephone communication between the provincial capitals of Jiangsu, Zhejiang, Anhui, Jiangxi, Hunan, Hubei, Henan, Shandong, and Hebei, and to expedite the transmission of information, Minister of Communications Zhu Jia-hua ordered Yan Renguang, Director of the Department of Telecommunications, to contact Tang Baoshu, Director of the Postal Savings and Remittances Bureau, to borrow 800,000 yuan in order to complete the telephone service as soon as possible. According to Shen Shi News Agency reporters yesterday, this loan has been generally agreed upon and a contract will be signed soon for the release of funds.

Building a Long-Distance Telephone Network for Nine Provinces 142

The long-distance telephone network for the nine provinces, with Nanjing as the center, plans to build five main trunk lines to connect the telephone communications of the nine provinces. The so-called five main trunk lines are (1) the Jinghan Line, from Nanjing via Wuhu, Anqing, and Jiujiang to Hankou. This line is busy with military, political, and commercial communications, and it is planned to install three pairs of copper wires. (2) The Jingjin Line, from Jingdupu, via Xuzhou and Jinan, to Tianjin. It is also planned to install three pairs of copper wires. (3) The Jiqing Line, from Jinan to Qingdao, has two pairs of copper wires, and it is planned to add one pair. The cost of replacing the poles along the line is high. (4) The Xuzheng Line, from Xuzhou along the Longhai Road to Zhengzhou. (5) The Hanchang Line, from Hankou along the Wuchang Line to Changsha. Due to the simple telephone traffic on the above two lines, it is planned to install one pair of copper wires each for the time being, and it is also planned to install various boosters in suitable locations in the nine provinces to facilitate direct telephone communication between the nine provinces.

Contacting the Postal Savings Bureau for Investment 143

In addition to the construction of the five main trunk lines by the Ministry of Communications and various equipment along the lines, it is also necessary to add two pairs of copper wires for the Shanghai-Hangzhou trunk line and along the Beijing-Hangzhou highway. The total cost of all necessary expenses has been estimated by Hu Ruixiang, Director of the Nine-Province Long-Distance Telephone Engineering Office, to be 5 million yuan. In addition to borrowing 200,000 pounds from the Gengkuan, equivalent to 3 million national currency, and raising another 1.2 million yuan from the Ministry of Communications, an additional 800,000 yuan has been borrowed from the Postal Savings and Remittances Bureau to promote its completion. Director Yan Renguang and Director Tang Baoshu have met several times to discuss the loan. The Postal and Telecommunications departments have generally drafted the loan contract. Shen Shi News Agency reporters learned yesterday that the main terms of the contract include (1) a long-distance telephone loan of 800,000 yuan for the nine provinces; (2) an annual interest rate of 1%; (3) the income from the Department of Telecommunications and other businesses is long-term stored at 100,000 yuan as a guarantee for principal and interest repayment; (4) after the completion of the five main trunk lines, it will be repaid in six years. The above main terms have been generally agreed upon, and once they are submitted to the Ministry of Communications for approval, they can be formally signed.

The Tongde Steamer Escapes Danger 148

Encountered a Storm in Huangshi Port

Now Has Sailed to Shanghai

The Tongde steamer, managed by the Dafang Foreign Firm, which was transporting coal to the Yangtze River, was blown to the side of the river by a strong storm in Huangshi Port. The hull was stranded, and the anchor chain was lost, causing huge losses. It has now escaped danger and will return to Shanghai for major repairs. The details are as follows:

Met with an Accident in a Strong Storm 149

The Tongde steamer is owned by the Tongde Company and managed by the Dafang Foreign Firm. Recently, it sailed from Shanghai to Pukou, loaded with more than 2,000 tons of coal, and sailed to Huangshi Port, downstream of Hankou, for unloading. Upon arrival, it encountered a strong storm, and the ship was unable to berth. The shipowner dropped anchor, but the storm blew the ship to the Yangtze River about 30 miles upstream of Huangshi Port. The hull was pushed to the side of the river, trapped in a shallow beach, and lost its ability to move.

Sending a Barge for Rescue 150

The shipowner urgently telegraphed Shanghai for help. The company, realizing that the steamer was deeply embedded in the sand and could not be towed, dispatched a barge to the scene of the accident. They planned to gradually offload the coal from each hold to lighten the ship's draft, then tow it to the center of the river. The offloaded coal would be transported to Huangshi Port. The steamer would also be towed to Huangshi Port for overall repairs, in preparation for its return to Shanghai for further repairs.

Returning to Shanghai for Major Repairs 151

The Tongde steamer encountered danger, breaking its anchor chain. The loss is estimated at six to seven thousand yuan. Adding the costs of offloading cargo and towing during the grounding, the total loss reaches over ten thousand yuan. The Shanghai office has telegraphed instructions to sail to Shanghai. After investigating the truth of the accident, passenger claims will be processed. Meanwhile, it will enter the dock for major repairs and have its anchor chain replaced. The telegram received yesterday stated that the Tongde steamer should arrive in Shanghai within three days.

Unit Should Be Added After Numbers in Chinese Telegrams 163

Units of Numbers Such as "Jin," "Yuan," "Hao," "Liang," etc., Will Be Implemented Uniformly Nationwide Starting September 1st

In order to reduce the burden on the public for sending telegrams, the Ministry of Communications previously formulated the "Measures for Writing House Numbers and Various Numbers in Arabic Numerals in Chinese Telegrams." The measures stipulated that numbers (such as five thousand six hundred seventeen yuan and seven jiao) could be written as (5617) yuan using Arabic numerals, and charged as two characters. It was also stipulated that if the meaning of the numbers in the context proved that they were indeed representing the quantity of silver or commodities, there was no need to add unit words such as "jin," "yuan," "jiao," or "pieces." For example, the sentence "Remittance (5000) yuan" could omit the word "yuan" and be written as "Remittance (5000)." Since implementation, the various sectors have saved a lot of money when sending Chinese telegrams. However, some merchants have overused the measure of omitting units, resulting in numbers appearing one after another in a brief telegram. Due to the omission of all units, it was impossible to determine whether they were codes or plain text. According to regulations, coded telegrams are charged double. Senders, seeking to simplify the number of words, made the telegram very similar to a code. However, if charged as a code, the telegram fee would increase. Therefore, misunderstandings often arose between the sender and the telegraph office. The regulations, originally intended to facilitate the public, became the main cause of disputes. Therefore, the Ministry of Communications specially issued an order to amend the original measures. According to an official of the Shanghai Telegraph Office, the ministry order has been received and will be implemented uniformly nationwide from September 1st. The main idea of the amended articles is that units must be added after Arabic numerals in Chinese plain text telegrams, such as (345) jin, (6.78) yuan, etc. If the units such as jin and yuan are not specified in the telegram, the entire telegram will be charged as a coded message.

Customs Regulations on Salt Content in Imported Mordants and Chemicals 165

Imports with More Than 20% Salt Content Are Generally Prohibited

The Jianghai Customs issued a notice yesterday regarding the salt content in imported chemicals and dyes. The notice stated: "It has been found that imported mordants and other chemicals contain salt. The Customs Administration of the Ministry of Finance has now stipulated that the content of sodium chloride (i.e., table salt) is limited to 20%. The following measures should be followed immediately: (1) All mordants and other chemicals containing more than 20% sodium chloride (i.e., table salt) are generally prohibited from import. (2) All mordants and other chemicals containing 20% or less sodium chloride (i.e., table salt), regardless of whether the ingredient is an unclean impurity or intentionally added, are allowed to be imported without restriction. All merchants should be informed of this matter. This notice is hereby issued."

The Nanshi Rent Reduction Association Petitions Party and Government 174

The Shanghai Nanshi District Rent Reduction Committee, since its establishment, has been under the leadership of party discipline and entrusted by the citizens. It has taken reasonable and legal measures and received the sympathy of landlords who understand the general situation. As a result, rent reductions have been gradually resolved. The difficulty lies in the fact that tenants demand rent reductions from landlords and declare that they have deposited the rent in the bank, but the landlords turn a deaf ear and still file lawsuits for rent arrears. Although the court cannot bear to completely disregard public opinion, it still ignores the evidence of tenants' demands for rent reductions and the evidence of deposits in the bank based on the landlords' one-sided statements. As a result, they seek peace but feel uneasy. The rent has not been reduced, but the burden of litigation has increased first. They demand cost savings, but are forced to open up new sources of income. At this time, it is only possible to publish a special edition of the Shanghai Rent Reduction publication to gently appeal, hoping that the public will be enlightened and save the precarious Shanghai. Due to insufficient funds, a small fee of two jiao per month is charged for printing paper, which has been understood by the party and government. Now, for the sake of widespread publicity, the fee has been reduced to one jiao, but it has been envied by those who are jealous. In desperation, all branch meetings have decided to unanimously stop paying rent and deposit the rent in the bank. A large-scale petition will be held on September 1st. The petition has been temporarily postponed after Shen Xinwu, a standing committee member of the association, discovered that it was the anniversary of the Communist Party. The petition is recorded below, appealing for the decline of the municipal situation and the deterioration of people's livelihood, requesting rent reduction to alleviate the people's difficulties and revitalize Shanghai. Since its establishment, the association has been under the leadership of party discipline and entrusted by the citizens, proceeding cautiously and appealing in an orderly manner. Although a few landlords who understand the general situation have reduced rents in consideration of commercial difficulties, there are also many who seek only profit and disregard the people's suffering, and some who wait and see without seeing clear documents. If this drags on, there will be more problems, and the relationship between hosts and guests will be damaged, leading to more disputes over rent reduction. In the recent situation, shops are deserted, and court courtyards are as crowded as markets. Although it has been repeatedly stated that the rent is deposited in the bank, summonses for rent collection continue to arrive, and judgments for eviction follow one after another. If a solution is not urgently sought, it will inevitably lead to bankruptcy and closure, and Shanghai's merchants will be almost wiped out. Therefore, in desperation, we unite all the district branches in the city and appeal to the authorities to consider the situation in Shanghai and the suffering of merchants, and request the implementation of rent reduction according to the precedent of Anqing, the capital, so that merchants can survive and seek recovery. We dare not make a moaning without illness, but deeply feel the pain and appeal.

War Scars Visible, Wounds Felt Deeply 181

Zhabei Gradually Recovering Prosperity

A Conversation with Wang Binyan

Zhabei has suffered deeply from the January 28th Incident. Although the municipal authorities and local elders have been working hard on its reconstruction, there is a trend toward gradual recovery. A reporter from the Datong News Agency has made a special record of the situation below.

The Idea of a Tramline Has Been Around for a While 182

Yesterday morning, a reporter from the Datong News Agency went to the residence of Wang Binyan, of the Shanghai Northern Business Community, on Meiyuan Road, Zhabei, and personally interviewed Mr. Wang. He was granted an audience, and the reporter first asked if he had heard about the Municipal Public Utilities Bureau's plan to build a tramline in Zhabei, as reported in the newspapers. Mr. Wang said that the plan to operate trams in Zhabei did not start today. Last spring, Lu Bohong and Xu Chunrong (founders of the Nanshi Water and Electricity Company) strongly advocated it and asked me to join them as initiators. Later, because the municipal government already had a complete plan for the reconstruction of Zhabei, Mr. Lu and others thought that the government's undertaking would certainly be more perfect than a commercial one, so they did not want to overstep their authority, and the matter became quiet.

Route Plan Thorough and Extensive 183

Mr. Wang continued, saying that the route planning for the tramline was very complete at the time, including Datong Road, Gonghe Xin Road, Zhongshan Road, Baoxing Road, Baoshan Road, Qiujiang Road, etc., forming a circular route. At the same time, it also crossed Zhongshan Road to connect with the trams in Nanshi, and another line was opened directly to the city center. Whether the current route plan of the Municipal Public Utilities Bureau adopts the original plan, I cannot guess. However, this move is of great help to the revitalization of northern Shanghai.

Scars Still Visible, Prosperity Gradually Recovering 184

The reporter then asked Mr. Wang about the reconstruction of Zhabei after the war. Mr. Wang replied that Zhabei has been scarred since the January 28th Incident. However, with the assistance of the municipal authorities and the efforts of the Zhabei merchants, the morale of the people and the state of the market have shown a good recovery and prosperity. Recently, the Commercial Press factory building on Baoshan Road, of which the undamaged portion, the company has been mending. This act has been very impressionable to the residents of Zhabei, so the houses destroyed by the war between Baoshan Road and Baoxing Road are being built one after another, and construction is booming. If we can continue like this, it will be able to restore its former appearance in no more than two or three years.

Tax Revenue Recovering to Former Levels 185

The Datong News Agency reporter then went to the Municipal Northern Tax Collection Office on Datong Road and met with Cao Xinchu, a clerk in the collection section. When asked about the tax revenue situation, Mr. Cao said that the office is responsible for the seven districts of Zhabei, Wusong, Jiangwan, Zhenru, Tangqiao, Yinhang, and Pengpu. Jiangwan and Yinhang districts have suffered more from the war, so tax revenue is still sluggish. Tax revenue in Zhabei and other districts is gradually recovering to the pre-war state. Before the January 28th Incident, property tax revenue was about 240,000 per quarter, but now it has gradually recovered to about 200,000. Other taxes, such as entertainment tax, have recovered to the pre-war collection amount. However, stall taxes are only about 60% of what they were before, which suggests that the wounds of the coolies have not yet healed. However, due to the recent opening of the land price tax and the transfer of tobacco and alcohol license taxes to the municipal government for collection, as well as the implementation of the slaughter tax, the total monthly income is about 120,000 yuan, which is even more than before the Shanghai war.

The Two Roads Bureau 186

Facilitating Passengers at Hangzhou Station

Contract Signed with Longfei Company for Shuttle Service

The Traffic Department of the Two Roads Bureau, recognizing the large number of passengers traveling to and from Hangzhou Station, specially contacted the Hangzhou Longfei Automobile Company to arrange shuttle services for passengers, in order to facilitate travel. The two parties negotiated a draft contract, which was submitted to the Roads Bureau for formal signing and has now been implemented. The contract stipulates that the Roads Bureau allows the Longfei Automobile Company to shuttle passengers only to and from Hangzhou Station. This operating franchise cannot be transferred. However, if the company violates the contract, its franchise will be revoked after three warnings from the Roads Bureau. If the company wants to terminate the contract midway, it must give advance notice and stop providing vehicles only after a replacement contractor has been found. The car fare within the city shall be in accordance with the agreed price, and the long distance shall be in accordance with the price stipulated by the Zhejiang Provincial Highway Bureau, and the passengers are not allowed to solicit tips, and so on.

Monks and Taoists Returning to Secular Life 187

Not Allowed to Take Temple Property

Order from the Ministry of Interior to the Buddhist Association to Comply

The Chinese Buddhist Association received an instruction from the Ministry of Interior yesterday, which read: "The case was approved by the Hebei Provincial Government No. 200, based on the report from the Director of the Department of Civil Affairs, based on the report from the Joint Civilian Education Association of the Chinese Buddhist Association in Ji County, Yu County, and San County, requesting an interpretation of whether monks and Taoists returning to secular life can take away property purchased under the name of the monk or Taoist. Please forward this request for review." The reply was approved. "After investigation, it was found that if the property purchased under the name of a monk or Taoist was purely operated with the surplus of temple property, it should still be regarded as the property of the temple. When monks and Taoists return to secular life, they cannot take it out of the temple." The Association is hereby ordered to instruct its members to comply with the regulations.

Municipal Police Bureau Sets Deadline 188

For Collecting Fees for Honor Guard Permits

No Continuation of the Old System from the Qing Dynasty Allowed

Implemented Starting September 10th

The Director of the Municipal Police Bureau, Wen Hongen, stated that residents of this city often overspend on weddings, funerals, and celebrations. Some even continue the old system from the Qing Dynasty, forming parades that are bizarre and varied. This not only wastes money and fosters extravagance but also damages the national image. Lawyers Zhang Yifan, Yao Yongli, and Fu Ganghou arrived at court early, and the gallery was full. After Judge Zhan Liangce took his seat, lawyer Yao Yongli stood up and requested permission for Zhu Maocheng, a member of the Shanghai Municipal Council's Traffic Committee, to express his opinion. He then immediately announced the verdict: "Zheng Fa'zhu and He Wushan (i.e., He Liansheng) are each sentenced to three months of imprisonment for the crime of jointly instigating others to use violence and coercion to obstruct others from exercising their rights. The rest of the defendants are found not guilty. Zhu Fengxiang, Cang Gongwen, and Zhu Shuqiao are all found not guilty." Before the judgment is finalized for Zheng and He, the number of days of detention shall be used to offset one day of imprisonment for every two days. The Shanghai Municipal Council's lawyer, Ru Bao'yi, immediately declared that he would waive the right to appeal for the defendants who were declared not guilty and released them immediately. Zheng and He both expressed dissatisfaction and must file appeals. During the appeal period, they requested permission to post bail. The court checked the tickets and ordered Zheng and He to each post a bail of 400 yuan to be released.

Therefore, thirteen measures have been specially formulated to banish bad habits, and have been submitted to the municipal government for approval, and will be implemented from September 10. The announcement and measures are recorded below.

Announcement 189

The Public Security Bureau issued Announcement No. 22, stating: "It has been found that residents of this city often use honor guards for weddings, funerals, and other events, and some even violate the ban and continue the old system from the Qing Dynasty, or contain feudal colors, adding splendor and dazzling the eyes, forming teams to parade through the city, without feeling strange. This old habit not only wastes money and fosters a culture of extravagance, but also damages the national image. In order to banish bad habits, this bureau has drafted measures for issuing permits for honor guard parades, which have been submitted to the municipal government for approval and ordered to be followed. It is now scheduled to be implemented from the tenth of this month. In addition to reporting and notifying the subordinate agencies to comply, the attached measures are hereby announced to the citizens of this city for compliance. In the future, for weddings, funerals, and other events, unless the etiquette is simple and no honor guard is used, all honor guard parades that march on roads or pass through the jurisdiction of this city must apply to this bureau in advance for an honor guard permit in accordance with the aforementioned measures, and are not allowed to use honor guards containing feudal colors. Those who dare to violate this regulation will be severely punished."

Measures 190

1. For weddings, funerals, and other events in this city that use honor guard parades that march on roads or pass through the jurisdiction of this city, a permit must be obtained from this bureau in accordance with these measures before they can pass.

2. To apply for a permit, the host or his representative should come to the bureau in advance to obtain an application form, fill in each of the following items, and the permit will be issued after review by the bureau: (1) Name, age, place of origin, address, and occupation of the applicant; (2) Reason for the application and the date and time of the honor guard parade; (3) Starting and ending points of the honor guard parade and the route it will pass; (4) Types of honor guards and the number of people accompanying them (excluding guests); (5) Number of bands hired and their names and addresses.

3. The number of honor guard members shall not exceed 300 each time.

4. The permit fee will be charged according to the number of honor guard members, as follows: (1) 50 people or less, 2 yuan; (2) 51 to 100 people, 4 yuan; (3) 101 to 150 people, 6 yuan; (4) 151 to 200 people, 8 yuan; (5) 201 to 250 people, 10 yuan; (6) 251 to 300 people, 12 yuan.

5. Simple wedding and funeral etiquette that does not use honor guard parades is not subject to these measures.

6. The following honor guard costumes are strictly prohibited from use: (1) Lanterns and ceremonial objects with official titles; (2) Qing Dynasty costumes and yamen runners' clothing; (3) Flags, gongs, umbrellas, and other items containing feudal colors; (4) Honor guards that hinder good customs.

7. The band for the honor guard parade should hire those who have obtained a registration certificate from the Social Affairs Bureau (this measure will be handled in accordance with the regulations after the deadline for band registration by the Social Affairs Bureau).

8. If there is any change in the route, it should be reported in advance for approval and should not be changed temporarily.

9. The permit should be carried by the applicant during the honor guard parade for inspection by the police along the way.

10. When this bureau issues a permit, it will notify the police station in charge to send a police officer to accompany and protect the parade until the end.

11. The permit should be returned to the bureau for cancellation after use.

12. Those who violate any of these measures will be dealt with separately in accordance with the following provisions: (1) Those who violate Items 1, 2, or 9 shall be immediately prohibited from passing; (2) Those who violate the provisions of Item 4 by reporting more than the actual number of people shall be fined double the amount of the permit fee; (3) Those who violate one of the provisions of Item 6 shall be immediately detained or confiscated separately; (4) Those who violate Item 8 shall be immediately stopped.

13. These measures shall be implemented after being submitted to the municipal government for approval and promulgation.

Mutual Lawsuit Between Fu Xiao'an and Yan Dajue 192

Final Arguments Concluded Yesterday

Verdict Scheduled for the 31st

Fu Claims No "Activities" to Return to Shanghai After Pardon

Yan Claims Ordinary Warning, No Intimidation

Fu Xiao'an, a Ningbo native and general manager of the China General Chamber of Commerce Bank, recently engaged lawyers Dai Chengxiang and Qin Liankui to file a complaint in the First Special District Court against Yan Dajue, a Cantonese lawyer, for intimidation. The reason for the lawsuit was that Dai Zhenwu, the owner of the Dai Shengchang Steamship Company (who had become a Japanese citizen), owed the China General Chamber of Commerce Bank tens of thousands of yuan. Fu filed a lawsuit with the Japanese Consulate, and the result was a judgment that Dai should repay 73,000 yuan in foreign currency. Dai then claimed that this amount was Fu's "activities" fee, and negotiated with Fu. He also stated that his lawyer, Yano, was a Japanese citizen and could not appear in a Chinese court, so Yano appointed lawyer Yan Dajue as his sub-agent and sent a letter to Fu Xiao'an stating the facts, saying that Fu should compensate all the reputational and financial losses suffered by him and should reply clearly within five days, otherwise he would file a criminal lawsuit. After receiving the letter, Fu believed that lawyer Yan had engaged in intimidating behavior and therefore filed a lawsuit. The court had already interrogated the case once and ordered the two parties to try to reconcile outside the court. These details have been recorded in this newspaper. Yesterday afternoon, this case was further examined by Judge Liu Yugui in the Ninth Criminal Court. Fu Xiao'an also personally surrendered to the court. According to Fu, as the general manager of the China General Chamber of Commerce Bank, after receiving the letter from lawyer Yan, which stated, "I should compensate for the loss of reputation and money, and reply clearly within five days, otherwise I will file a criminal lawsuit," I thought that this kind of thing was worthless, so I ignored it. Unexpectedly, after a few days, there was another registered letter from lawyer Yan, saying that if I still ignored it, I would definitely file a criminal lawsuit. In order to safeguard the commercial reputation and understand the truth, I asked a lawyer to reply with a letter. Unexpectedly, after receiving the two letters from lawyer Yan, rumors suddenly arose, saying that I was engaging in malfeasance and embezzlement. There are more than a thousand employees in my bank. If I remained silent and did not defend myself, it would be as if it were true, so I had to surrender to the court and file a lawsuit. Moreover, I have never met lawyer Yan before, so there is no enmity between us. It is really because this matter has too much impact on society and the banking industry that I cannot remain silent. Moreover, I have lived in Shanghai for decades. I returned to Shanghai from Dalian in 1931 after receiving a pardon. There were no "activities" with the Nationalist Government and asking Dai Zhenwu to find a way to raise this small amount of tens of thousands of yuan. As for Dai Zhenwu, because he had dealings with the Hongkou branch of the China General Chamber of Commerce Bank, there were a total of three account names, one was Dai Zhenwu, the second was Zhenjiang Dai Shengchang, and the third was Shanghai Dai Shengchang. Because of the outstanding bank loans, I filed a lawsuit with the Japanese Consulate, and a judgment has now been made to repay the amount. Now the defendant, lawyer Yan, without asking the truth of the matter, rashly sent a letter of intimidation based on the empty words of the Japanese lawyer Yano, so he should be punished according to the law. When asked, the defendant Yan Dajue claimed that when I sent the first letter, I did not know if the plaintiff had received it, so I registered the second letter with the post office, but the wording inside was exactly the same as the first letter, and the drafts of my letters were all reviewed by lawyer Yano. Therefore, this matter was originally handled by Yano, and I was a sub-agent. Moreover, the words in the letter were all ordinary warnings, asking him to reply clearly, and there was no intimidating behavior at all. Therefore, the plaintiff's lawsuit this time is actually of a slanderous nature, so I filed a counterclaim. Then, the plaintiff's lawyer, Qin Liankui, stated that the mediation of this case was unsuccessful. Judge Liu ordered the debate to begin. The plaintiff's agents, lawyers Dai and Qin, stated that this case is divided into two points: a private prosecution for intimidation and a counterclaim for slander. Regarding the private prosecution, Article 1540 of the Judicial Yuan's instruction to the higher courts of all provinces and regions on July 5, 1932, states: "If a crime or tort is committed by an agent, he shall not be exempted from liability because he is an agent. However, recently, there have been cases where people have published announcements or statements in newspapers in the name of representing others, and if there is any damage to the reputation of others or other illegal circumstances, the agent is not responsible because of his status as an agent. This view is a misunderstanding. In the future, when such incidents occur, the courts should investigate and deal with them according to the circumstances and in accordance with the law. If the court believes that the defendant has committed a crime or a tort, it shall not be considered that he is naturally not responsible because he is an agent. Therefore, all courts are hereby notified, and all subordinate courts are hereby instructed." In this case, whether the defendant's act of sending a letter to the plaintiff in the name of Dai Zhenwu constitutes the crime of attempted intimidation should be clearly judged. After investigation, it was found that the letters issued by the defendant were all his own claims and were not based on Dai's commission. Therefore, the defendant should be responsible. As for the counterclaim for slander, according to the provisions of the criminal law for the crime of slander, it is necessary to know that the facts are false and accuse them to the official government before the crime of slander can be constituted. Now the facts of this case are all there, how can it be called slander? It should be refuted. Then, the defendant's lawyer, Sheng Peidong, argued that the occurrence of this case was due to lawyer Yan Dajue being commissioned by Yano to send a letter to Fu Xiao'an on behalf of Dai Zhenwu. According to Fu's accusation that the letter was intimidating, saying that "if you do not reply clearly within five days, I will file a criminal lawsuit," the establishment of the crime of intimidation requires two elements: (1) there must be an intimidating act that causes the other party to feel fear; (2) there must be an intention to illegally obtain the property or illegal interests of others. Now, reading the letter issued by lawyer Yan, it only says to reply clearly within five days, otherwise I will file a criminal lawsuit. It can be seen that there is no intention to illegally obtain the property or illegal interests of others, but only to express that he wants to ask the court for a proper solution. Moreover, lawyer Yan, according to my instructions, is a legal agent, and the issuance of letters is in accordance with the procedures. How can it be called joint intimidation? According to the above situation, there is no doubt that he is venting his anger on the defendant and is determined to frame him. The private prosecution should be dismissed and a counterclaim for slander should be filed. Judge Liu reviewed the report and ordered the debate to be closed. The verdict is scheduled to be announced at the afternoon of the thirty-first of this month.

Hongxiang Xing Factory Builds Its Own Trawler 198

Can Be Completed and Applied in November

The Daily News reported that Chinese fishermen mostly used sailboats to fish more than a decade ago. The fishing methods were old-fashioned. Later, under the advocacy and guidance of the fishing industry, they successively built fishing vessels and used machines to catch fish, but the vessels built were not new-style and had very little horsepower. Therefore, most of the fishing vessels in the various fishing areas now are old and dilapidated vessels from many years ago. It is now known that the Hongxiang Xing Machinery Shipyard in Pudong, this city, built its own newest type of trawler in April of this year. The vessel is 135 feet long, 23 feet wide, and has 600 horsepower. The internal machinery is all made of pure steel, which is strong and durable. Since the start of construction, most of the work has been completed. By the end of November of this year, it will be completed and applied. It is reported that after the vessel is completed, the factory plans to sail into the coastal areas to catch fish and is currently applying to the Ministry of Industry for registration and licensing.

Ningbo Industrial Bank 199

Enthusiastic Application for Small Loans

In recent years, idle capital has concentrated in cities, leading to the accelerated decline of rural areas and the phenomenon of abnormal urban development. After the financial sector absorbs idle capital, it often invests in real estate construction and various speculative businesses. Therefore, although cities appear to be increasingly prosperous on the surface, the expansion of these non-urgent needs has a significant direct impact on people's livelihoods because it fails to organize and regulate the absorbed idle capital. In view of this, the Ningbo Industrial Bank of this city has specially established a small loan department to provide loans in order to regulate the economy of the middle class and below in this city. Since its opening, in less than ten days, the number of people who have gone to the bank to obtain articles of association and application forms has reached hundreds every day. From other places, such as the Beijing-Shanghai and Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo lines, and even as far as Henan and Hankou, several letters are sent every day to request the articles of association, which shows that small loans are an essential plan to support industry and commerce today. It is now known that after investigation, more than 300 households have been qualified after review. Since receiving the bank's notification, they have been processing the formalities one after another, and the borrowers are all very happy. It is also heard that the bank has newly established a national product revolving collateral loan to support the production and sales development of national product industry and commerce. Recently, many people have been going to the bank to negotiate mortgages.

Public Works Bureau Stipulates New Regulations for Public Automobiles 201

The Public Works Bureau has now added a new clause to the license regulations for public automobiles, that is, a mirror must be installed on the car. The size and position must allow the driver to clearly see the vehicles behind in the mirror. This clause will be implemented from January 1 next year. In addition, the regulations on freight vehicles have been slightly revised, namely (1) those with a load of 12,000 pounds (gross weight) or less must be fully equipped with car tires. However, those who have been approved to use solid tires and have been issued a license in the past are not subject to this restriction. (2) Those with a load of more than 12,000 pounds but not more than 16,000 pounds must be fully equipped with car tires. However, those who have been approved to use solid tires and have a license in the past are not subject to this restriction. In addition, vehicles that have been delivered on a regular basis and are awaiting license are also excluded, but they must be registered with the donation office before September 29. The above new regulations will also be implemented on January 1 next year.

Fourth District Detective Team Cracks Down on Repeat Offenders 208

Confiscates One Handgun and Six Hand Grenades

Confesses to Robbery Cases, All Verified by Victims

At about 10 pm the night before last, Li Guiqing, a detective from the Public Security Bureau of the Fourth District of Zhabei, received a tip that bandits with guns were committing crimes in the Jiaotong Road-Zhongshan Road area. The handgun number was checked to be 7806. After being taken to the district, one of the bandits confessed his name was Wu Hongtu, 25 years old, from Yancheng, living in a shack on Jiaotong Road, unknown door number. Another bandit named Dong A'gen, 21 years old, from Ningbo, living in a shack on Gaolang Bridge, Yangshupu. Another bandit named Wei Guihe, 29 years old, from Funing, living in Xujiazhai Road, Chaomi Beach. The old woman was returning to Jiangbei with 130 yuan, but the old woman did not come, so they gathered there to discuss. Only the bandit wives Li Gu's, 22 years old, wife of Li Xiaowuzi, and Wu Shen's, 25 years old, wife of Wu Hongtu, were arrested. Lin Anding, the owner of Rihui Port, said that at about 10 am on the first day of this month, he took 800 yuan in one-yuan notes, 450 yuan in five-yuan notes, and 200 yuan in jiao notes, totaling 1,400 yuan, from the wholesale store on Sijing Road to distribute wages to the factory. When he was more than ten steps away from the factory building, he was stopped by bandits and robbed of all the banknotes. The interrogating official believed that the robbery cases confessed by the bandits were all verified by the victims and ordered them to be sent to the Public Security Bureau for interrogation.

Resumed Work in the Afternoon After Persuasion

After persuasion by the police and the factory, the entire workforce returned to work at 2 pm.

Reading Questions and Answers

How to Strive (Continued) 219

丨丨 Reply to Mr. Zhang Yiyan 丨丨

The second question also reveals Mr. Zhang's inclination towards a formalistic view. One should consider personal life prospects and those of the masses as an integrated whole. A person with lofty ideals would never abandon practical life to merely dream about "ideals." Having "ideals" doesn't mean discarding the "mundane"; on the contrary, ideals can only be realized through reality. Many people, seeing that reality isn't as bright as their ideals, try to escape it. Such people not only fail to realize their ideals but end up compromising with reality, or else they're left with mere fantasies. During the Xinhai Revolution, some people thought that engaging in revolution was equivalent to becoming a monk, and that having a job meant you couldn't simultaneously be revolutionary, or that you should first quit your job. But they still claimed revolution as their ideal. They formally separated revolution from practicalities. Of course, revolution requires organizers who must dedicate themselves to it, but such individuals should only comprise a small fraction of the revolution. The vast revolutionary masses are all simultaneously "scrambling for food" and striving for their ideals. The goals of personal survival and striving are inherently conflicting! Moreover, if one abandons reality to engage in empty talk about revolution, success may never come. The same applies to seeking knowledge. Vocational skills, literature, and social sciences can be learned according to one's actual life circumstances. We've recently discussed this in an article titled "Learning Theory and Learning Technology." Because Mr. Zhang separates life from ideals, he arrives at an abstract decision to "first pursue literature, then social sciences," completely disregarding vocational skills. By the time he's about to "starve," he "has to abandon literature or social sciences and focus on life-sustaining skills." Although this cannot be called a complete failure, it undoubtedly involves a formalistic logical error. Mr. Zhang fails to integrate the study of literature and social sciences into practical life. Why not study literature and social sciences while also learning life skills? Why not maintain one's basic living while striving for one's ideals? These things are not absolutely opposed to each other; one makes them absolute.

Mr. Zhang also says, "I must try my best to squeeze into the ranks of the masses, but first I need to temper my muscles and bones and train my knowledge." While this seems correct in general, it's still a fantasy. We don't temper our muscles and bones first before joining the ranks of the masses, nor do we prepare our knowledge well before entering the world to work. We can only temper our muscles and bones in the life of the masses, and only in practice can we gain true knowledge. To resist Japan, we can do so anytime, anywhere, in any profession. It's not necessary to quit our jobs and run to the Northeast to resist Japan. Studying why Japan wants to invade China first before resisting Japan – this viewpoint, if not sly, deliberately deceptive, is simply too naive.

If that's the case, we naturally strive to lower the standard of our private lives and advance towards the path of ideals. Naturally, this process is a continuous battle, achieving our goals step by step with difficulty and hardship. How can personal demands be unmet to the point of "hindering our future and undermining our will"?

As for the third question raised by Mr. Zhang, saying that he "cannot bear the different stimuli, making him uneasy at work," and getting red in the face after seeing "a young man who committed suicide due to economic oppression," this is entirely driven by emotions. While we cannot "turn a deaf ear" to such things, it's not something to be dismissed with a fit of anger. These stimuli should only make us understand reality more clearly; how can they hinder the progress of young people?

In summary: We believe Mr. Zhang's attitude is very sincere and straightforward, worthy of special respect. But Mr. Zhang, like us, is still someone who has enough to eat, so all his views inevitably carry the atmosphere of our somewhat middle-class lives. In reality, there is no road in the world; roads are opened up by people. How to strive can only be suggested in principle and method by others; how to walk it depends entirely on your life practice. We have said this repeatedly 丨. We hope Mr. Zhang reads this letter while also reviewing previous articles, to quickly overcome his depression and find the path to strive.
