Xiaoxitian (Little Western Heaven) 220

— By Zhang Henshui

First Episode: Ghost Battle: A Remote Traveler from Guanzhong Comes; Destitute Family: Four Farmers Cross a Ferry; Hanging the Masses

As he spoke, he jumped out of the car. Two porters immediately came forward to carry his luggage. Mr. Zhang and Mr. Li followed him in and saw a two-story courtyard house. Below the building, there were several brick rooms, while the upper floor was entirely made of wooden pillars and wooden walls. When people walked on the upper floor, the floorboards and walls vibrated with a "dong dong" sound. According to the porters, they would move their luggage to the two rooms downstairs. Li Shilian shook his head repeatedly, saying: "This is not good." The porter said: "Then, let's move it to the bungalows in the backyard, but the price will be a bit higher." Zhang Jiefu said: "Five dollars a day?" The porter smiled and said: "Not that much, a dollar and some cents is enough." Zhang Jiefu said: "A dollar and some cents, what's the big deal?" The porter, hearing this and seeing their situation, realized that they were clearly political figures, perhaps truly not caring about the money, so he carried their luggage and led them to the backyard. In this courtyard, there was a row of bungalows built with brick walls, with two rectangular glass windows in the front and back, and a half-glass door. This could barely be considered a Western-style house. Li Shilian first stretched his head to look at the hotel rules hanging on the wooden wall. The room rate was one dollar and twenty cents. He immediately planned in his mind that he would stay here for at least a month. For a long-term stay, if not a 30% discount, perhaps an 80% discount could be obtained, one times seven is seven, two times seven is one dime and four cents, adding up to just ninety-four cents. Looking at the room, there was a black wooden table, two chairs, two square stools, and an iron bed that was 70% new. Relatively speaking, it was still acceptable for settling down, so he told the porter to settle the luggage and shared a room with Zhang Jiefu. Because he had already checked in, the first thing the porter did was to bring a blue cloth duster. Li Shilian initially did not know what it was for until he saw Zhang Jiefu standing in the courtyard using the duster to dust off the dirt from his body, then he understood. Indeed, in this northwestern region, the first thing to do upon entering is to dust off the dirt. (9)

Fortress Against the Wokou 221

— Xu Jie

In the thirty-third year of the Jiajing reign (Emperor Shizong) of the Ming Dynasty, the Wokou (Japanese pirates) invaded the provinces of Zhejiang and Jiangsu, committing adultery, murder, and plunder. The people of our Zhejiang and Jiangsu suffered greatly at the hands of the Wokou. Their aim in disturbing our country was akin to piracy, without the ambitions of the Japanese of today. By the forty-second year of Jiajing, the Wokou had captured Pinghai, but Qi Jiguang defeated them, and eventually the pirates were pacified.

Qi Jiguang was a meritorious official who suppressed the Wokou; this is known to all. However, at that time, there were many people who killed Wokou in various places. Tongzhou, Suzhou, Ningbo, and other places also raised soldiers to resist alongside the government troops. Because the people felt the impact of this menace, they could not rely entirely on the government. Many fortresses still exist in various places as memorials to the resistance against the Wokou.

Like the Guanhaiwei of Cixi, a small city. Song'ao of Fenghua, bordered the Jiashan Port to the south, so there was also a fortress. At the foot of the White Pagoda Bridge in Mudu, Suzhou, there was an enemy watchtower, thirteen zhang wide and thirty-six chi high. The tower base was made of white stone, and the walls on all sides were built of bricks with various patterns. There were many small holes used for shooting bullets. The surroundings of the tower were picturesque, and the scenery was very beautiful, said to be one of the ten scenic spots of Mudu; it is unknown how many Wokou were killed there at the time.

Originally, at this time, the Wokou harassed from Fengqiao to Mudu, Xishan, and other places, burning, looting, and plundering along the way, committing all kinds of atrocities. Military commissioner Ren Huan and General Tang Kewan led troops to attack and suppress them. The Wokou fled into Taihu Lake, disturbing the east and west Dongting. Later, they disturbed Lingyan. Ren Huan led troops to catch up, killing many bandits under this enemy watchtower. Now, Chairman Chiang Kai-shek is using the "fortress policy" in Jiangxi to suppress the communists, which has yielded great results. I wonder what good methods we will have in the future to resist foreign insults? We, as ordinary people, should also "prepare for a rainy day"!

Old Tales of Conscription 223

— Sun Choucheng

The other day, I read Mr. Rong Yu's "Song of Joining the Army," which contained the line, "But those conscripts had very short lives, because they looked down on the corruption of the Green Standard Army, and the Green Standard soldiers couldn't stand their arrogance. Stationed in the same place, they often engaged in械斗 (xiè dòu, armed brawls) over trivial matters. The court at that time ultimately did not like the new style, so it disbanded them," which is slightly inconsistent with the facts. I, Choucheng, was one of the conscripts at the time, and know the details more clearly. I will now recount the situation as follows:

In the spring of the thirty-second year of the Guangxu reign, Jiangsu implemented conscription, recruiting more than 1,500 people from the three prefectures of Su, Song, and Tai. After arriving in Su, because the barracks across the river from Xiyuan were not completed, the teams were stationed in old barracks and temples inside and outside the city, organized into the First, Second, and Third Battalions according to the three prefectures of Su, Song, and Tai, called the Second Standard of the Jiangsu Army. The Green Standard Army north of Baodai Bridge was called the First Standard. (The barracks of that Standard were demolished during the "128 Incident" [Shanghai War of 1932] to rebuild an airfield.) I belonged to the First Platoon of the First Battalion of the Second Standard, serving as the deputy head of the eighth squad (initially there were no squad heads), in charge of fourteen people, stationed in the Lao Lang Temple in front of the Zhenfu Envoy's Office. At that time, those who were conscripted from the three prefectures had varying levels of education. There were scholars who had entered schools, students who were in school,纨绔子弟 (wánkù zǐdì, spoiled rich kids), and hoodlums. Wearing yellow cloth uniforms, they swaggered through the streets, local hoodlums avoided them, and donkey cart drivers treated them like gods, calling them "Conscript Lords." After dinner, the platoon leader and officers led the team on long-distance marches in the streets and alleys, all singing the military songs "Advance, advance!" and "The brave men of the world contend for merit," along the way residents supported the old and led the young, leaning on their doors to watch. The First Standard Green Standard Army still had black cloth wrapped around their heads, wearing numbered gowns, and had to hold a three-foot-long numbered sign when going out. Comparing the two, there was indeed a world of difference. The governor of the time, Chen Kuilong, accompanied by the three chief officers of the Training Office, often gathered the conscripts to give speeches, so they all knew to pay attention to military discipline. One day, someone in the Third Battalion of the Second Standard encountered soldiers of the First Standard outside the Yang Bridge at the Daxu Gate, holding numbered signs and flirting with prostitutes on the road, believing that it was disrupting military discipline, and stepped forward to stop them. They were looking for trouble because the superiors were treating the First and Second Standards unequally, so they took this opportunity to return to the barracks to incite trouble, went out in groups to pick a fight with the conscripts, and beat anyone they encountered. Eventually, two people were robbed and beaten to death outside Fengmen. Later, two ringleaders were captured from the First Standard, executed at Wang Fei Ji to avenge the drowned. What Mr. Rong Yu called械斗 (xiè dòu, armed brawls) probably refers to this incident. After entering the barracks in the winter of that year, management became stricter. About 70% of the people from the three prefectures deserted because life was too hard. The authorities had no way to solve this problem, so they recruited people from the Xuzhou, Huaizhou, and Haizhou areas to fill the vacancies. At that time, I had already been admitted to the Army Attached School. Three years later, when the conscripts were discharged, there were only about a hundred people left, so what Mr. Rong Yu called disbanding is not accurate. I am afraid that the matter has been forgotten for a long time, so I specially make it public.

The Misty Record of Imperial Fragrance 224

— Originally written by Princess Der Ling of the Qing Dynasty, translated by Qin Shouou

The duties of the Imperial Guards were not easy! Although their task was to protect, patrol, and guard, their actions had to be very careful. First, they could not talk and laugh loudly, and second, they could not make too much noise while walking, otherwise they would inevitably face the danger of having their heads chopped off at any time. Therefore, after the Empress Dowager rested, the surroundings were as silent as death. Although we could vaguely see the lights of village homes in the distance flickering on the horizon through the car windows, no human voice was heard, not even the barking of dogs or the chirping of insects. The air was filled with a solemn and cold atmosphere, like ice. Under this rare atmosphere, our Empress Dowager spent a very comfortable night.

The next morning, the Empress Dowager got up. She usually got up very early, and now that she was on the train, her spirit was even more excited, and she got up especially early. After getting up, she quickly washed and dressed, and then hurriedly ordered the train to start. Thus, this yellow train set off in the faint morning light. Not long after the train started, it suddenly began to rain, but not heavily, just a very fine drizzle. If we were walking in this rain, even without an umbrella, our clothes would definitely not be soaked; at most, they would feel slightly damp. This kind of drizzle is most common in spring, often falling several times a day, probably due to the season?

This season is "Qingming" (Tomb-Sweeping Day). The saying, "During Qingming, the rain falls in torrents," is truly a most accurate descriptive poem. Every Qingming Festival, we descendants must bring wine, food, paper money, etc., and respectfully go to our ancestors' graves to perform the tomb-sweeping ceremony. This is a custom that is common everywhere in China. Therefore, when our train passed through the wilderness, we saw countless people along the way, braving the rain, worshiping at their ancestral graves. They were all very far away from the railway! (118)

Can such a broken umbrella cope with the coming storm?

— Yi An

Mosquito 225

— (Yang Yusheng)

Mosquitoes in the twentieth century are truly cunning! In the past, people only knew that mosquitoes could fly, but now they have evolved to be able to climb!

In the deep recesses of the bed curtains, they can creep in, lying on the less sensitive parts of the human body, sucking blood. These are the top-notch characters!

Secondly, although their creeping skills are lacking and difficult to make them intimate companions, their senses are very keen. They know the head and foot positions of the target object in the tent, lurking outside and waiting. The head or feet cannot be said to have no contact with the bed curtains, so their bellies are often full!

Although the skills of the top-notch characters are high, the dangers they face are also great; this is in line with the old saying "The higher you climb, the harder you fall." When the target object wakes up, sees many transparent, blood-colored "balloons" staying on the top of the tent, the concept of revenge is aroused, and he immediately sentences them to the extreme penalty of "exterminating their clan." At this time, each of them dragging a "saturated" belly, loses their spirit of flying and climbing, and ends up in a crushed and broken end!

Where I've Travelled

Summer at Yellow Crane Tower 226

— Shazhou

Like floating clouds, five years have passed so imperceptibly, but every summer, I think of Yellow Crane Tower.

Speaking of the Yellow Crane Tower itself, those who have visited it all know that it is not as beautiful as one imagines, but since it has become a famous scenic spot, it cannot be without merit. So when our ship arrived in Hankou two hours later, I made a pilgrimage to this medieval relic. At this time, although I did not have the elegant sentiments of the ancients who climbed to a high place to compose poems, I was extremely emotional at the moment of leaning on the railing and looking down, and what was even more pleasant was that I decided to spend the summer at Yellow Crane Tower. Of course, this cannot be as simple as officials and celebrities going to Mogan Mountain or Qingdao, and there are naturally various inevitable reasons mixed in. It is not that I have that extra money, nor that I have such a leisurely time, but it is a long story, and it is off-topic, so let's put it aside for now.

So I said, that summer I lived on the Yellow Crane Tower. After getting up early in the morning, I walked past that famous Goose Character Stele. When I walked past it for the first time, I didn't feel how powerful this goose character was written. I only felt that Wang Xizhi was really joking. Fortune-telling halls and photo studios are even more special products of the Yellow Crane Tower. Generally, Chinese people are so rich in poetic sentiment that after applying their names to the scenic spot, they also sigh that the scenic spot is hard to revisit, and they need to leave a photo of a hermit under the flowers. Therefore, in order to adapt to this need, more than twenty or thirty photo studios have opened on the ridges and slopes of the small Yellow Crane Tower, which can also be said to be ah, flourishing. Speaking of the fortune-telling halls, there are even more horizontal plaques askew, calligraphy and paintings all over the walls, bright windows and clean tables. The self-proclaimed hermit sits in the middle, waiting for someone to send money to dissolve misfortunes. There is also a park behind the Yellow Crane Tower. The cement railings in the memorial hall in the park have not been repaired. I think the reason for this lack of repair is probably the same as that of an old bronze teapot. I remember that there was a legend about someone who played antiques and bought a bronze stove from the Tang Dynasty in the market one day. He happily invited relatives and friends to appreciate it together. Who knew that a woman said that she did not know the goods, saying that the bronze stove was dirty and crooked, and there was nothing good about it, but the owner heavily declared that the good thing was that it was dirty, and if it were not dirty, would it be an antique? The valuable thing is this bit of dirt. Naturally, the woman would retort that the dung board is also very dirty... However, I dare not say more here. What I want to say is that the decline of the memorial hall is probably the reason why it is a famous scenic spot.

The room I lived in was rented to me by a famous photo studio, upstairs. Looking out the window, you can see a panoramic view of Wuchang, and turning your neck, you can also see Hankou emitting black smoke, as well as the large and small ships moving in the river. But I am really afraid of doing this, because when I look down, the streets are full of hot sun, and hurried pedestrians walking in the sun. I really don't understand, I don't understand why life is always so busy? And I don't know what people are so busy with?

The tourists on the Yellow Crane Tower are almost endless from morning to night, but the men or women who are parasitic on this scenic spot also exist at all times. Beggars with broken legs cry and bump their heads on the ground, kiln girls with too much powder always use that disguised method of pulling people, dealing with tourists like soldiers dealing with villagers, and photographers are even more competing with each other, only the fortune tellers are leisurely, but who can guarantee that he is not worried about life and his intestines are tangled and his eyes are piercing?

Scenic spot, scenic spot!

There is no clean land in this world.

Chinese Economic Society 230

Eleventh Annual Meeting Record

(3)

Shao Yuanchong's Speech 231

Following Shao Yuanchong's speech, "Economic Control and Ability Control," he stated that the issue of economic control is a significant problem in China today, amidst internal strife, external threats, and the destruction of the rural economy. Therefore, the general theme of the annual conference is "Discussion on the Implementation of Economic Control Policies in China." Now, he would like to expand on this topic, namely, economic control and ability control. At first glance, these seem to be two separate concepts, but they are actually complementary. When discussing the meaning of economic control, it refers to the national economy and the people's economy. In reality, a certain plan is needed, such as the government running enterprises alongside the people running enterprises. This is the inevitable path to developing a country's economy and advancing human society. Ancient economics were tribal, and the economic conditions of social organizations were extremely simple. As times progressed, economies entered a state of competition, adopting competitive strategies. In this process, the small were no match for the large, and the unorganized were no match for the organized. Therefore, the small and unorganized gradually disappeared. In modern times, economic power has expanded even further. In addition to its own development, it can also manipulate politics, diplomacy, international trade, etc. Therefore, the political power of the United States does not reside in Washington but in the New York banking community. They can use their monopolistic economic power to influence politics. That's why Europeans are reluctant to engage in politics and prefer to engage in economics. In the past, when he visited the United States, he found that the organization of economic groups was extremely rigorous and extensive. For example, they have consultants on transportation laws, etc., which greatly help in reducing transportation costs and various legal matters. Even in congressional elections, the group pays close attention to the investigation of candidates, providing economic assistance to those who, after being elected, can help the group's economic activities and standpoints, so as to ensure their election, or else undermine them. From this, it can be seen that economic power has a significant impact on politics. In addition, powerful economic groups can grasp finance, currency, and the market, making them suitable for the various economic needs of the people. Therefore, economic control, which is related to people's lives, is guided and assisted by the government. In many European countries, related enterprises are all controlled and regulated by the government, so that these countries can achieve prosperity and strength. In China's recent situation, economic control is particularly urgent. For example, various raw materials for national defense and commodity raw materials are shipped abroad at cheap prices. Due to the failure to control agricultural products economically, the suffering and impact on the people are enormous. Regarding these issues, we, from the standpoint of scholars, study whether a controlled economic plan can be implemented and achieved. Otherwise, the plan is equal to zero. From this, a second question arises, namely, that while the economy needs to be controlled, people's abilities should also be controlled. Therefore, the advancement of a certain undertaking must require certain people with the necessary knowledge and conditions before it can proceed smoothly. Conversely, even if there is a plan but no capable talent, how can one expect to achieve the desired results? Knowing the methods to solve problems and being able to implement them is ability. Using a small amount of effort to achieve great results, using few methods to do more work and achieve greater results, this is what is called ability. For example, person A studies politics, person B studies economics, and person C studies engineering. If their respective fields of study are mutually transferred to handle unknown undertakings, then the results will definitely be nil. If they are assigned according to their studies, then they will surely be able to demonstrate their abilities. For example, if he does not understand a certain undertaking, he should first study it with time, so that he can understand it before taking on the task. If so, then time is wasted, and the wheel of time keeps moving forward. By the time he finishes learning, time has passed, and what he has learned is not useful. Doing things in this way consumes a lot of energy and yields very little results. Therefore, to solve the problem of people's livelihood through economic control, one should also consider the expression of people's abilities. Great talents should be used to do great undertakings, and small talents should be used to do small undertakings. In this way, all kinds of people can use their abilities. Time is not wasted, and the result of joint efforts will be very grand. Therefore, when talking about ability control, (1) emphasis should be placed on education and training, which can be divided into higher and ordinary. Ordinary people should be made to serve in ordinary undertakings, while higher talents should be made to handle higher undertakings and pay more attention to basic factual training. For example, in the social aspect, statistics must be implemented, so that one can know the location of higher and ordinary talents at home and abroad, and use them at any time to exert their abilities. (2) The problem of ability distribution: when talents and undertakings are both available, distribution is extremely important. For example, if specialists and ordinary people are distributed according to their abilities, then at least their abilities can be fully utilized in their undertakings. The above principles, when applied to economic control, are not only not contradictory but also complement each other. Therefore, in terms of land and labor, land belongs to the economy, and labor belongs to ability. This meaning can be expressed mutually. The controlled economic plan set by the British Liberal Party in 1928, such as industrial control and financial control, belongs to the economic aspect, while labor control belongs to ability. Therefore, economic control not only involves itself but also requires consideration of all aspects, so that all people in the country can use their abilities on a large scale and in a wide range to do what they can do, without wasting their labor, energy, and time. If one day is devoted to doing one thing with one's ability, then the results of that thing will be great. If one day is devoted to doing several things, then one's ability will be insufficient, and the results will be minimal. Proceeding according to the above questions, the solution to the problem of economic control can be expected to be realized, and doing things in this way should also achieve very good results, and so on.

Hu Shuhua's Speech　Lastly, the chairman invited Hu Shuhua, the president of Hunan University 232

to speak. Hu, due to time constraints, gave a brief speech, saying that there is a wonderful mutual assistance between academic groups and academic institutions, and the beauty of complementing each other. The natural disasters and man-made disasters that our country has suffered in recent decades have caused the economic environment to fall into a state of stagnation. Sun Yat-sen said, "People's livelihood is the center of social evolution." How to make society evolve and how to develop people's livelihood is a heavy responsibility for all of you. This time, your society has taken "Discussion on the Implementation of Economic Control Policies in China" as the topic, which shows great insight. The results of the discussion will be a powerful contribution to the whole country. In addition, with the permission of President Ma, students from the Department of Political Economy of our school will be able to attend and listen, and the benefits will be considerable. As for our school's lack of material resources and simple equipment, and the lack of hospitality, Shuhua, in addition to welcoming you, would like to express his apologies. The meeting adjourned at about five o'clock. After the meeting, photographs were taken, and various statistical charts of the Hunan Agricultural Experiment Field were visited. At six o'clock, they went to Jingyi Hall of Hunan University, where Hunan University hosted a dinner. The second day of the annual conference was decided to be devoted to reading papers, and in the evening, they went to a night banquet at the West Route Headquarters of the Bandit Suppression Army of Jiangxi, Guangdong, Fujian, Hunan, and Hubei.

Jiangsu Education Expense Office 235

Letter to the Education Expense Committee

Revised Regulations for Handling Tooth Tax and Slaughter Tax and Bidding Regulations

The Jiangsu Education, Funds Management Office, for the purpose of revising the tooth tax handling regulations and bidding regulations, and the slaughter tax implementation rules and bidding regulations, sent a letter to the Jiangsu Education Funds Committee for record. The original letter briefly stated that the tooth tax should be handled by inviting merchants to contract, in accordance with the slaughter tax method. The previously drafted handling regulations and bidding regulations were sent to your meeting for deliberation and approval. However, the previously set bidding date was based on the fiscal year, uniformly stipulated as June 15th. It has now been changed to bidding at any time. The financial bureaus of various counties have long been abolished, and the two-thousandth revenue section of the Finance Department has been replaced by this office to collect and remit the funds. All of these have changed, and there is a need for revision. In addition, merchants with excellent performance in handling the tax are allowed to continue for another year to become proficient. Tooth tax and slaughter tax have been handled in this way for many years and have been quite effective, and should also be included in the regulations so that there is a basis. Therefore, the tooth tax handling regulations and bidding regulations, together with the slaughter tax implementation rules and bidding regulations, have been revised accordingly and sent to your committee for inspection and record.

Ministry of Education Stipulates 240

Standards for Science Equipment in Secondary Schools

The Municipal Education Bureau Relays Orders to Secondary Schools to Comply

The Shanghai Municipal Education Bureau issued an order to all secondary schools in the city, stating: It has been received from the Ministry of Education's Order No. 8083 that, according to the statistics of the graduation examinations of secondary school students in various provinces and cities in recent years, the academic performance of science teaching in various secondary schools is relatively poor. The Ministry has already informed and ordered improvements to be made. The improvement of science equipment is closely related to the improvement of science teaching. There has been no uniform standard for the preparation of science instruments and medicines in various secondary schools. The organizers often have no basis to follow, and it is difficult for educational administrative agencies to assess. Therefore, the Ministry has specifically ordered the Committee for the Compilation of Curricula and Equipment Standards for Primary and Secondary Schools to develop science equipment standards for secondary schools. The currently compiled standards include secondary school physics equipment standards and secondary school chemistry equipment standards. The standards include detailed explanations and thorough regulations on the equipment for student experiments in chemistry and physics at the high school level, such as lists of instruments and medicines, demonstration experiment equipment, factory equipment, and attached drawings. In addition, there are minimum equipment standards, ordinary equipment standards, and complete equipment standards, as well as estimates of the value of instruments and medicines, so that each secondary school can purchase them separately according to its economic capacity and gradually improve and enrich them. After the implementation of these standards, not only should each secondary school comply with the equipment matters, but also the educational administrative agencies, supervisors, or specialist inspectors of each province and city should use this as a basis in actual inspections. Each bureau should also follow these standards to improve the science equipment of its subordinate secondary schools to enhance teaching effectiveness and improve student levels. In addition to being announced by the Ministry, the bureaus should also be ordered to inspect and distribute 20 copies of each of the standards. The order is issued so that you are aware of the contents of the order, and one copy of each of the secondary school physics and chemistry equipment standards is enclosed for reference.

The Problem of Civic Education in National Revival (1) ·Zhang·Yuan·Ruo 250

丨Lecture at the 4th Shanghai Summer Lecture School丨

Introduction

Distinguished guests, I am very pleased to be here today at the invitation of the Shanghai Municipal Bureau of Education to give a lecture. The weather today is too hot, and I don't want to waste your time with unnecessary words. The topic I want to talk about today is "The Problem of Civic Education in National Revival."

There are probably several motivations for me to talk about this topic. First, you are all people engaged in education, and the purpose of this school is specifically to study various educational issues. I lack specialized research in pedagogy, so I dare not talk too much about educational issues. However, I am a person who studies political science, and everyone knows that political science and education cannot be completely separated, especially the issue of civic education, which has a deeper relationship with political science. Secondly, I have a very important reason, which is that in recent years, whether in lectures or writing, I have had a central idea, which is nationalism. Therefore, I dare to say that at least I myself must believe that I am a thorough and ardent believer in nationalism. Therefore, I feel that the issue of civic education in national revival is very important, so I take this opportunity to contribute some opinions to everyone. Furthermore, I remember that I gave a very simple talk on the essentials of civic education at the Public Education Center last week. At that time, due to time constraints, I did not have time to elaborate. I have long wanted to supplement it. Today I have the opportunity to study it with everyone in more detail, which is very gratifying.

1. The Importance of Civic Education

I feel that the most important driving force for the survival of a nation is its citizens. According to the principles of political science, the composition of a country has three elements: one is territory, one is sovereignty, and one is the people. And I believe that the most important of these three elements is the people. Because territory and sovereignty must be maintained and protected by the people. If there are no people, or even if there are people, but the people do not have sound strength, then the so-called territory and sovereignty will inevitably exist in name only. Therefore, the people can be said to be the only element of a country.

So, how can we truly make the people the only element of a country? This requires us, who are responsible for education, to train them. Then they can truly have a relationship with the country. The Chinese nation has reached an unprecedentedly dangerous and difficult period at this stage. During this extremely dangerous and difficult period, there are certainly many ways to save the country, but the most important and fundamental thing is to rely on the people who are the only element of our country. However, can the Chinese people now have a close relationship with the country? Can they have the strength to maintain the territory and protect sovereignty? And do they have the courage and sense of responsibility to maintain the territory and protect sovereignty? These are all extremely serious problems that urgently need to be remedied.

Superficially, the Chinese people are numerous, with as many as 400 million. No other country in the world can compare with China. Logically speaking, having so many people should generate tremendous power. But in fact, it is not so. China is a country without power in the world. Take Belgium, for example. It is one of the smallest countries in the world. Its territory is only about the size of a few counties in China, but it was able to resist its powerful neighbor during the European War, the most powerful army in the world, Germany, which is enough to prove that although the country is small, its power is very strong. China has always been known to the world for its vast land, abundant resources, and large population. Why is it powerless? Why is it so declining and facing such a serious national crisis? I am the least fond of flattering others, and I am also the least willing to belittle my own nation. Someone from a certain country, I will not name him for the time being, said something that neither hurts nor itches us. He said that although China has 400 million people, it is impossible to find a sound citizen like those in Europe, America, or Japan among these 400 million people. These words are certainly too contemptuous of us, belittling us, and insulting us, but if we humbly reflect on it, we should also be deeply vigilant. It is undeniable that there are very few people in our country who possess the qualifications of sound citizens. It is precisely because there are not many truly sound citizens in China that the country cannot generate power, and the spirit of the nation is also declining day by day.

Therefore, the most important plan for saving the country in the future is to start with training citizens, training citizens to make each of them generate power, and striving for the country, so that each of them has a close relationship with the country, and condenses with the country. In this way, 400 million people will have the power of 400 million people. Otherwise, the people will have nothing to do with the country, and the people will not know that there is a country in their minds. Not only will they not know how to fulfill the responsibilities of citizens to the country, but they will also hinder the survival of the country and overflow the rights and interests of the nation. This kind of person who has nothing to do with the country and even hinders the survival of the nation cannot be regarded as a citizen of the country, and cannot generate power for the country. Therefore, if we want to save the country, we must first train all 400 million people in the country to become citizens, which requires promoting and popularizing civic education. In the simplest terms, civic education is to educate the people to know how to fulfill their responsibilities as citizens to the country, so that the people and the country become one. In this way, one citizen can generate the power of one citizen, and the power of 400 million people can be gathered into a most powerful force. With this great power, we can solve the unprecedented national crisis and create a new life for the nation.

Cotton Yarn 264

Small Actual Delivery Volume of Cotton Yarn for August

2,400 Bales of Yarn at 181 Yuan 265

2,100 Dan of Cotton at 35 Yuan 266

The August Gold Rooster brand yarn was listed on March 1st this year. The opening price for the first session was 181.6 yuan. At that time, due to disappointing spring sales, weak US cotton, pressure from foreign firms, and the huge inventory of over 100,000 bales of yarn in Shanghai, there was extreme panic and strong selling pressure. The lowest price reached around 172 yuan. Later, in mid-June and July, the factories found it difficult to sustain due to high original costs and increasing losses. A major factory, Fengchao, suffered the most. As a result, various factories, recognizing the unfavorable situation, suspended or reduced production, leading to a contraction in output. At the same time, yarn sales in South and North China began to recover, and the market sentiment gradually improved. Merchants from Tianjin, finding coarse yarn cheaper than Japanese yarn, purchased large quantities in Shanghai. More recently, the financial community profited greatly from flour and wheat, and also absorbed large quantities of branded yarn. The highest market price reached 187.5 yuan. Unexpectedly, as the market price rose, there were more sellers, and actual demand suddenly turned dull. Short sellers delivered 1,000 bales of new goods. Free Talk

Superior 279

— Cang

Being superior to contemporaries is not too difficult. Whether as a poet, novelist, playwright, or any kind of professional, this is indeed true.

Because there are originally not many "giants" in the current literary and artistic circles, it is easy for someone with a little talent to emerge. As someone said: In a land without birds, even bats are pleasing. So "literary figures" and the like easily become famous.

Fame is essentially empty, it exists based on one's career. Anyone who wants to achieve what they are doing will have no time to make themselves famous, and no energy to care about their fame. If their fame is detrimental to their career, they will escape fame, hide their name, and despise it. Just like a runner with the trophy in front of them, they will have no time to care about the spectators or look back at their fellow runners.

As for deliberately making oneself look a little better to please everyone, originally seeking fame and fortune, that is the "pandering to the world" type, also called "deceiving the world." It is also easy to become famous, because there are not many "giants" among appreciators and critics. Or there are giants, but for other reasons, they do not speak, letting them make noise.

Many newly famous writers originally had great hopes, but they made themselves very pitiable simply because of their love of fame. So, they are afraid of offending their masters, so, they are afraid of being out of touch with the times, and even more so, they are afraid of not looking like a certain ideology or school. Going along with the times, making a living under the whims of the times, the result is that they become like specimens in a science laboratory, labeled as XX professional, unable to soar.

People can never obliterate their own emotions, so they cannot be indifferent to praise and criticism, but too much concern is not good, it is better not to care. Seeking revenge for every complaint and laughing at every praise is such a great extravagance and damage, such as advocating essays and writing "Crossing the River," discussing the mass language and complaining about flying tiles, all of which are detrimental to "spirituality." Fame is a burden!

A Painful Memory in the Desert 280

— Cao Lengquan

In that scorched earth and desert of the Northwest, I endured eight years of hardship. I experienced the prolonged drought of three or four years, and all kinds of strange changes. Many compatriots died tragically because of this, and I was still able to eke out a living, and I really felt extremely fortunate. In those times, I often thought: "The Northwest doesn't have enough food to eat, and I still came to eat!" Therefore, any extravagant hopes also disappeared.

From 1927 to 1934, the Northwest never had a good rain. The vast plains and hills, with red faces, seemed to be angry, and it was difficult to see a little green plant. The scorching sun fiercely emitted its fire, determined to burn everything on the ground to death. Sometimes, a sudden gust of wind would rise, and the sky would be filled with dust and sand, turning yellow as far as the eye could see, making people suspect that the end of the world was coming.

The tens of millions of people suffering from disasters still struggled and fought desperately with nature for survival. They drew sweat from dozens of feet deep wells to irrigate their fields (in various parts of the Northwest, it was often necessary to dig dozens of feet to get water). Finally, it was like pouring a cup of water into a hot pot, it could not help but evaporate all at once! The seedlings were withered, and the sweat was shed in vain. The scorching sun tormented them, causing them to die in the thousands and tens of thousands. Death was their only relief.

1929 was the year of the most severe disasters in the Northwest, with drought, cold, war, wolves, and rats. In addition, there were hungry soldiers searching for grain from house to house, and the hungry wolves came out of the mountains in groups to prey on humans and livestock.

Flour was three jins for a dollar, and coal was seven jins for a dollar. Human resources were so scarce. Therefore, many people used political power to deprive others of their lives in order to preserve their own. Helpless victims slept on the streets, eating yellow earth to barely survive. I have also witnessed it myself.

In mid-December of that year, the sky, which had not rained for a long time, suddenly had a heavy snow, and crows and sparrows froze to death in flocks. In the evening, those homeless victims often huddled together in groups of three or five in front of people's doorways, and by the next morning, they had died in piles there. If you were not careful, you would often bump into a zombie. Therefore, some people often piled snow in their doorways to prevent victims from sneaking in to sleep! The compassion of mankind was extinguished!

In that heavy snow, the sacrifice of life was truly unknown. The surviving victims with frozen hands and feet could be seen everywhere in Xi'an City. They were in rows and columns, some with the muscles on their hands and feet already rotten and peeling off, and the joints were still connected like human bone specimens. Some had completely frozen off their limbs, and the red and swollen flesh revealed white bones. Their limbs were so painful that they dared not touch the ground, sitting and wailing miserably.

Hunger, severe cold, scorching heat, and the exploitation of officials and gentry accelerated the destruction of that group of people's lives. At the same time, the warlords' wars often caused panic. In those three years, in Shaanxi Province alone, it is said that three million innocent people died tragically in this way.

Such a tragic sacrifice is even more painful than the group in Serafimovich's "Iron Flood." However, it is just a tragedy, what is the price?

Literary Jottings 281

— Hua Yu

(6) Thus, writing became a rare commodity

Writing sprouted among the people, but later it was inevitably seized by those with privileges. According to the author of the "Book of Changes," "in ancient times, knots were tied for governance," so even tying knots was something for those who governed. When it fell into the hands of shamans and scribes, needless to say, they were all people below the chieftains but above the common people. As society changed, the scope of people learning to write also expanded, but it was mostly limited to those with privileges. As for the common people, they were illiterate, not because they lacked tuition fees, but because they were limited by qualifications; they were not worthy. Moreover, they couldn't even see books. In China, before block printing became developed, a good book was often "stored in secret cabinets and copied in three libraries." Even scholars still didn't know what was written in it.

Because writing was something for those with privileges, it had dignity and mystery. Chinese characters are still very dignified today. We often see baskets with the words "Cherish written paper" hanging on walls. As for talismans used for exorcism and healing, they relied on their mysteriousness. Since writing contained dignity, then the person who knew writing also became dignified. New dignitaries emerged endlessly, which was unfavorable to the old dignitaries. Moreover, if too many people knew writing, it would also damage the mysteriousness. The power of talismans was because these things that looked like characters were unrecognizable to anyone except Taoist priests. Therefore, they were bound to control writing. In medieval Europe, literature and learning were all in monasteries. In Croatia (Kroatla), even in the 19th century, only priests were literate. The people's spoken language regressed to being just enough for their old lives. When they reformed, they had to borrow many new words from foreign countries.

In China, in addition to status and economic limitations, Chinese writing also had a high barrier for the masses: difficulty. If one didn't spend ten years or so on it, it wouldn't be easy to cross this barrier. Those who crossed it were the scholar-officials, and these scholar-officials tried their best to make writing even more difficult, because this could make them particularly dignified, surpassing all other ordinary scholar-officials. Yang Xiong of the Han Dynasty, who liked strange characters, had this problem. When Liu Xin wanted to borrow his "Dialects" manuscript, he almost jumped into the Huangpu River. In the Tang Dynasty, Fan Zongshi's articles were made so that others couldn't punctuate them, and Li He's poems were made so that others couldn't understand them, all for this reason. Another method was to write characters so that others couldn't recognize them. The inferior ones would look up a few ancient characters from the "Kangxi Dictionary" and insert them into their articles. The superior ones were like Qian Dian, who used seal script to write Liu Xi's "Explanation of Names." Recently, there was also Mr. Qian Xuantong, who copied "Elementary Learning Questions and Answers" for Mr. Taiyan according to the "Shuowen" character forms.

Writing is difficult, and articles are difficult. These were all originally so. On top of these, the scholar-officials deliberately added difficulty. Yet, they still wanted it to have a connection with the masses. How could that be possible? But the scholar-officials wished it to be so. If writing were easy to recognize and everyone knew it, then writing wouldn't be dignified, and they wouldn't be dignified either. People who say that vernacular Chinese is inferior to classical Chinese start from this point. Now, those who discuss the language of the masses and say that it's enough to teach the masses the "Thousand Character Classic" still have the root of their meaning here.

Expelled from the Palace of Art 282

— Shen Shengshi

When I was eight or nine years old, I became interested in painting. I still loved it in middle school. A drawing teacher once gave me the highest score in the whole grade. At that time, I planned to become a painter. Later, I finally got into an art school in Suzhou.

But as soon as I entered art school, I was dazzled.

Walking on the path of the Western-style building, staring blankly at those lively male classmates and beautifully dressed female students, listening to the piano and violin, my heart fluttered in the music wind.

Every day, walking into the school gate, gazing at a long rectangular plaque with the words "Palace of Art" Palace of art, a young and weak heart beat fast;

Oh, the magnificent and beautiful Palace of Art!

I heard the delicate classmates praising it so much.

So I lowered my head, timidly, and wandered in the Palace of Art.

What a charm it was to draw pictures by the green window! I enjoyed the happiness in the Palace of Art, as if I was slightly drunk, fluttering in the music wind, dreaming beautiful dreams, so I also grew my hair long and learned to be a painter.

But I came from the countryside, born in a poor family, after all, I was not worthy to enjoy the poetic life in the Palace of Art.

Finally, I was expelled from the Palace of Art.

Originally, I had taken the wrong path and should not have gone to the paradise of the sons and daughters of wealthy families.

My expulsion from the Palace of Art, I myself cannot explain what crime it was for. Does a rogue-like society have anything to say about the destruction of a youth? I have no defense. If a person does not die, he should work hard. One day, society will understand my cleanliness and frankness; but I should not have dreamed in the ivory tower. I understood that myself.

Without nostalgia, I walked out of the Palace of Art.

Goodbye! Delicate friends!

After waking up from the dream, deep pain attacked me. The rainy wind blew me like a flickering street lamp in the dusk, lost at the crossroads.

Vast world, where am I going? Wandering on the street at dusk, holding a cigarette butt, I am a young unemployed man!

Carrying confused sorrow, trudging on the indifferent world, confused like a journey in the dusk, I advise myself:

Having groped through the dark night, tomorrow may be a sunny day!

Carrying my twenty-one years of sad heart, groping on the dark road.

Being expelled from the Palace of Art, I have no regrets. Shaking off the tired spirit, walking out of the dark road stretching in the dusk, maybe it is my chance for a new life!

Remembering Lily Kobbe 283

— Xu Maoyong

One

Mr. Hui Tian sent the translation of "Lily Kobbe's Sleeping Shanghai." Reading it, it was completely different from when I was blankly facing the German original. I understood that this is how it was said. Then, I suddenly thought of Mr. Ren's words. He said that this girl! Mr. Ren always liked to call her girl—lived in Shanghai for more than ten days. Although she wanted to know the situation in China, she actually gained nothing. However, in my opinion, she already knew Shanghai very clearly. "Sleeping Shanghai" can be used as proof.

Now, she has gone to Beiping. Maybe there, she will recognize the face of China? In any case, I think her harvest from this trip to China will be more than Bernard Shaw's. As soon as Shaw arrived in Shanghai, he was taken by car to the salons of the wealthy, to see the faces of reporters and celebrities. Afterwards, he was still taken back to the ship by car. When he arrived in Beiping, he only ate at the general's mansion and looked down at the Great Wall from an airplane. The Great Wall was all he saw. What else did he see? Lily Kobbe, on the other hand, had ridden a rickshaw in Shanghai, been chased by dirty beggars, and been despised by the people in the third-class train. She had also been to factories in Zhabei and squeezed among the "wild chickens" near the Great World... Receiving the disdain of reporters, literati, and scholars, she ran around alone and actually discovered the secret core of Shanghai. When she arrives in Beiping, it will probably be the same, so she will know China.

It is said that in Japan, the police acted as her guide. If she wanted to see the lives of farmers, she would be taken to the magnificent living room of a landlord. In Shanghai, she did not encounter such a guide, so she felt very lucky. However, she did not know the reason. In fact, it was because Shanghai did not need such a guide at all. Japan is Japan, so the Japanese police have an obligation to cover up for themselves. But Shanghai is the Shanghai of China, ruled by Westerners. The police are supported by Westerners, and the shameful things in Shanghai only concern China's dignity, so the Western police don't need to cover them up. Moreover, the work of covering up ugliness can probably only be done in Japanese cities. In Shanghai, isn't there a canal full of "dirty water" below the aerial garden on the five-story building where "Mr. Willie" lives? And on the sampans in the canal, are Chinese coolies sleeping?

Lingering Fragrance 284

— TK

Younger Brother (5) 285

— Zhou Wen

Later, life became more and more difficult day by day, and the store could barely stay open. Mom told me not to study anymore, but to take advantage of having a relative who was an official in the army and go to him. As for my younger brother, he was already fourteen years old, so we could only let him study for two more years so he could manage the store, and Mom would have a substitute.

This day, when I was discussing it with Mom, my younger brother secretly listened for a while on the other side of the door, then went out to gamble without saying a word. Because it was New Year's, Mom didn't mind him. Sometimes I asked him:

"Younger brother, what school do you want to study in this year?"

"None of your business!" He paused for a moment and walked away with his big eyes.

After that, the shop assistants teased him:

"Little Zhou! You're still gambling; your brother is going to be an official!"

My younger brother put down his cards, glared his eyes, and said:

"I don't care, bah, being an official! You also call me Little Zhou, Little Zhou, damn you!"

"Look at you, you don't look like an official at all!" They still teased him.

"Damn your mother!"

Mom suddenly came out with a board:

"I don't believe it, can't I hit you just because it's New Year's! Humph, you want to be unruly, wait until I close my eyes!"

My younger brother was so angry that his eyes were straight. He poked Wang Er next to him, threw the cards, and ran away in a puff of smoke.

One day, a shop assistant told Mom that he had heard Wang Er next door discussing running away with my younger brother. Mom quickly opened the cabinet in the room to check. The money was fine, not touched at all. Then she quickly found a lock to lock it up. She thought he wouldn't dare to run away without money. Moreover, he had never been out before, so he and Wang Er certainly wouldn't know which way to go. She just had to watch out for him.

Talks

Miscellaneous Talk on the Ye Muhua Case 286

— Shou Peng

Since the Ye Muhua case occurred several months ago, our country's authorities have made absolutely no indication due to the state of national power. Although our consul in Nagasaki submitted a routine protest in the middle, it certainly did not obtain any key points. Originally, such a common tragic case had long failed to arouse the revulsion of the nation whose nerves were already paralyzed. If Ye Muhua had not returned to the country this time to appeal, I am afraid that this matter would have been permanently excluded from the memory of the nation. But the nation's sentiment of common hatred for the enemy has become so indifferent to this extent that it really makes one feel like the country is dying with each passing day, and feel neither like crying nor laughing!

During this so-called "emergency period," Japanese imperialists are frantically and actively preparing for war, especially for the invasion of China, which they are determined not to let go of. Since the Northeast was forcibly occupied, the so-called "Manchuria-Mongolia policy" has been desperately seeking its full realization. Therefore, aggression against China has become Japan's main task at present, and the seeds of invading China have been planted in the minds of every Japanese citizen. The idea of ​​hating Chinese people has also developed rapidly (it is a pity that some treasures are still chanting about "Sino-Japanese friendship"! ). The murder of Qi Muhua is not an accidental phenomenon, but a reflection of the ferocious face of the entire Japanese imperialist.

We still remember the telegram from overseas Chinese in Nagasaki appealing for the Ye case, which gave a bloody account of the tragic situation of Qi Jun's death at that time. Based on this bloody fact, the cruelty and inhumanity of the Japanese have been thoroughly exposed. Please see that after repeatedly seeking opportunities to insult and scold him for two consecutive days, he finally took out the seven-inch knife hidden in his chest and stabbed Ye Jun's left chest fiercely. This planned act of violence must have had considerable preparation in advance. According to reason and logic, it was obviously an intentional premeditated murder. The Japanese court has been protecting him in every possible way, using the excuse that the murderer has not reached the legal age and shirking responsibility and exonerating him is directly trying to cover the eyes and ears of the people of the world with one hand. Their vicious attitude will be more clearly seen by the world.

Before the "September 18th" Incident, the Japanese authorities repeatedly protested and threatened us under the pretext of the so-called "Nakamura Incident." Whether Nakamura existed or not, and whether he ever disappeared, even if he did, who should be responsible for this? All of this remains a mystery to this day. However, the Japanese used this incident as a pretext to further implement active military aggression, and then caused the outbreak of the "September 18th" Incident, forcibly occupying the territory of our northeastern provinces. Not long ago, Zang Ben disappeared in Nanjing. The way the Japanese dispatched ships to increase troops and threatened and intimidated us, if compared with the Ye case, one is intentional premeditated murder, and the other is intentional suicide to find a pretext for their certain attempt. The seriousness of the situation is already clear and obvious, and everyone knows it. "Humans with the same round heads and square feet, because of the strength or weakness of the country, the weight of the value of their lives is so different!" It is really regrettable.

The Ye case has occurred for a long time, and the nation has not yet made an appropriate expression. Ye's death is not a pity, but it is hateful that Ye died for the country and was humiliated. It is even more infuriating that the evidence after death is solid but it cannot achieve the purposes of punishing the murderer, compensation and apology! This case concerns the honor and disgrace of the entire country and the safety of the lives of overseas Chinese. If the national spirit of the Chinese nation has not yet been completely lost, it should swear to resist to the end. In recent years, our compatriots abroad have been humiliated, squeezed, expelled and massacred by foreign races everywhere. If the nation still does not rise up to struggle, strive to become stronger, and let others be the knife and ourselves be the fish, then in such a large area of ​​the world, there will never be a place for Chinese people to stand.

On "Literary Heritage" and "Foreign Stereotyped Essays" (Continued) 287

— Ming Tang

Now let's first look at his so-called sorting out China's literary heritage and accepting China's literary heritage. Is it "going to the camp of Chinese old literature to detonate bombs" and doing the work of disinfecting Chinese literature? The facts answer us, no. First, in the entire "Special Issue on Chinese Literature Research," we did not see an article, not even a single word, saying that their work was "going to the camp of Chinese old literature to detonate bombs" and doing the work of "disinfecting" Chinese literature. It exists in the second issue of the third volume of "Literature." However, this was after my so-called "foreign stereotyped essay" was discovered in the local supplement. Is this a later addition? Or did they forget it at the time? This is a bit difficult to figure out. However, they may say that this is because you don't have eyes, and we had already said it in a "veiled" way in the "Special Issue on Chinese Literature Research." Furthermore, this matter does not need to be stated explicitly. At this time, to propose to reorganize China's literary heritage and accept China's literary heritage, of course, it includes the meaning of "going to the camp of Chinese old literature to detonate bombs" and doing the work of "disinfecting" Chinese literature. Then I have nothing to say.

However, the fact is still the fact. When a thief takes someone's things, if someone asks, he will definitely say that he picked it up, or how he got it somewhere. Of course, he will definitely not say that I stole it somewhere. "Literature" very simply said at first that we want to reorganize China's literary heritage and accept China's literary heritage with new methods. Later, it added that this is "going to the camp of Chinese old characters to detonate bombs." Who knows that this must not be a thief-style evasive "excuse"!

However, the people of "Literature" are still worthy of our admiration. First, they proposed to reorganize China's literary heritage and accept China's literary heritage, which is to go to China's "old literary camp" to find the "gold sand" they need. Then they said that this work is "going to the camp of Chinese old literature to detonate bombs." At least, this point of dodging is already very "valuable."

Secondly, what "Feng" Jun is most proud of in attacking my article is saying that my article is a complete so-called "foreign stereotyped essay." This is very meaningful. "Feng" Jun said that my article is a "foreign stereotyped essay." In this way, all my words have been completely overturned by him. This is a very fierce, vicious and very clever way of saying it. However, anyone with clear eyes can see what kind of method this is. To put it bluntly, "Feng" Jun has only learned the most basic method of "putting a red hat" on others from a group of political secret agents. In my opinion, this method is really basic. Can "Feng" Jun say that because my article is a "foreign stereotyped essay," the reorganization of China's literary heritage and the acceptance of China's literary heritage proposed by "Literature" must be said to be a meaningful work no matter what? Can the gentlemen of "Literature" be so "bold"? The method of "putting hats" on people is now played too ordinary. Unexpectedly, for this small problem, the gentlemen of "Literature" also solemnly applied this most basic and contemptible method, which is a bit pitiful.

The most interesting thing is that although "Feng" Jun used all his strength to prove that my article was a "foreign stereotyped essay," he himself also fell deeply into the quagmire of "foreign stereotyped essay" at the same time. Not only is it a "foreign stereotyped essay," but it is also the most inferior "local stereotyped essay" that is more inferior than the "foreign stereotyped essay." Let's see: What is "Feng" Jun most proud of in that article? It's just some of the most boring "searching for chapters and excerpts" style of criticism on the text. May I ask "Feng" Jun, how much more brilliant is this than my "foreign stereotyped essay"?

The attitude of "Feng" Jun in writing that article is exaggerated and severe. This is probably because "Literature" is a magazine with a relatively high status in China, so their every move is "different from the public." My article was just written in a hurry, and it was revised by others, so there are indeed many unsmooth and procrastination points in the middle section. This is inevitable. I am not a "writer," so there are certainly many arguments in the text from time to time. We have never seen this kind of situation. Probably because "Literature" has a position, their writers must be "first-class" in logic.

Page 20

In fact, your things may not necessarily be able to dominate "China's literary world" now. There are many Chinese people with clear eyes, and their eyes are not looking at you now.

Finally, I want to advise the gentlemen of "Literature." I think it is better for you to quietly and peacefully do some work in picking "gold sand" from China's literary heritage. Originally, that is the place where you can "relax and enjoy yourselves." If you must hold the "gold sand" in China's literary heritage in one hand, and "detonate bombs in China's literary camp" in the other, it will be too disgusting to see. However, this is what the gentlemen of "Literature" are unwilling to admit frankly. Then forgive me for saying something "incisive," how did "Literature" continue to be maintained in the first place?

However, in the end, I still think that the gentlemen of "Literature" are worthy of admiration. It is because they can "pick gold sand" in one hand and "detonate bombs" in the other. At the same time, they can also "put hats" on people and quickly (perhaps they can already) learn the skills of political secret agents. This is where the gentlemen of "Literature" are far beyond us. My admiration for "Literature" lies in these two points. (Appendix: The second issue of the third volume of "Literature" was published on August 1st. It was not until about the 8th that someone told me that there was an article attacking me in it. Then I got sick again, so I was able to write an answer until today. I hereby state this).

The Sorrow of the Ghost 288

— Bu Yang

I don't know how long I was in a coma before I was awakened by a sad cry. This cry was strangely familiar, like my wife, like my daughter-in-law. He wondered why they were crying for no reason? But when he raised his eyes, he found several nuns performing the work of delivering him to the afterlife. The sound of the wooden fish rhythmically beat on his heart with the crying.

Am I dead?

He jumped up in a hurry, feeling much lighter. He looked at the bed, like a large mirror; lying inside was another self.

He didn't know when he was lying in the hall; he couldn't remember how he died! He wanted to ask his wife, ask his daughter-in-law, but they ignored him, as if they didn't recognize him at all.

Yes, he had entered another world. They couldn't see him, although he could clearly see them, but he couldn't let them know that he was standing in front of them.

He felt the sorrow of eternal separation.

Floating past his wife, past his daughter-in-law, past the nuns, he walked out of the hall and towards his home.

Under the corridor, he saw his three brothers talking about the cause of his death with red eyes, so he quietly sat on the empty chair opposite and listened.

From his brothers, he learned that he had died of a stroke, like his eldest sister, dying very quickly, in just three hours.

He also talked about his eldest sister, who was as fat as himself. She died when she was fifty-four years old. When he went to pay his respects that night, he saw her pacing around him in the bed.

Six nine fifty-four, dark nine, he always worried about it, fearing that he would not be able to pass that hurdle.

Now it was confirmed that he lived to the same age as his eldest sister and suffered from the same disease as his eldest sister.

Looking at the relatives and friends who had come from afar for him sitting in the courtyard and corridor, they all talked about his death with exclamation, and the sorrow, both indirect and direct, was smeared on everyone's face, deeply or shallowly.

His eyes swept across everyone's face, but he couldn't find his sons. They were far away in S port, and maybe they didn't even know he was dead.

His empty heart ached faintly, father and son were originally connected at heart.

Floating around the corner of the corridor, that was his home. He looked at everything in the room with attachment. His most beloved grandson was clamoring for hunger at this time. He pitifully said: "Grandpa is dead, no one will buy me things to eat?"

He happily walked over, stroking his grandson's head and kissing his grandson's face. He was surprised that no one paid attention to him when he was clamoring like that. He raised his eyes and found his basket placed by the bed, so he lovingly told his grandson: there are things you like to eat hidden inside, and pointed it out to him with his finger.

The grandson's clamor turned into crying. He didn't feel his existence and sobbed, "Grandpa is dead, no one will buy me things to eat?"

His heart was broken. In the eyes of his loved ones, he could no longer be seen, and in the ears of his loved ones, he could no longer be heard. He hated why omnipotent scientists did not invent a tool to convey thoughts between the living and the dead.

Thinking of My Hometown 289

— Jia

Suddenly, I thought of my hometown and couldn't help but sink into melancholy.

I haven't been back for several years. Long days drift by in a foreign land, like duckweed floating on water, stopping wherever is convenient, and gradually becoming accustomed to the life of a wanderer. The longing for my hometown has gradually faded, almost to the point of becoming a vague memory.

Sometimes, in a certain state of mind, a faint image of longing emerges, but these moments are rare. However, in my memory, my hometown is always beautiful and serene. Although I've been away for many years, people from my hometown often bring news, letting me know that it's not the dreamlike place I remember, but has undergone great changes, deteriorating day by day.

Yet, in my memory, my hometown remains a beautiful and cherished place!

The scenery there is hard to find here:

People's lives are full of joy and happiness. Early in the morning, little sparrows chirp on the pomegranate branches, singing their morning songs, without needing a clock to tell the time. Just hearing the crisp voices of the sparrows, everyone knows it's dawn and gets out of bed, each tending to their daily tasks. Women carry clothes and lead their children to the ponds outside their homes to wash them. The gurgling of the water echoes from the pond, mixed with laughter, like the music of dawn carried on the breeze. Children leave their mothers' sides and run freely on the grass, catching grasshoppers. When they catch one, they run joyfully back to their mothers, jumping and talking, expressing their happy and proud feelings.

It is truly a primitive and simple scene of local customs!

After washing clothes, they take their children home. The children walk ahead, singing folk songs, while the mothers follow behind, chatting and laughing. Every face bathed in the gentle sunlight is soft and cheerful.

Then, wisps of smoke begin to rise from the roofs of every house. After breakfast, the children go to school one by one, while the mothers do some light needlework.

The hometown I remember is so peaceful and beautiful, making one want to savor it endlessly.

But the reality of my hometown has probably destroyed this tranquility long ago!

And so, a dim picture weaves itself into my mind:

Many people have given up crying and wear faces of resentment and sorrow, living their lives in misery. Heavy clouds of life weigh down on their heads and hearts. Even when they gather together, they remain silent and listless. All kinds of worries have taken away their joy, and sighs and anxieties have replaced happiness. The cruel beating of life has made them lifeless, their bodies and minds withered.

Many have been forced to abandon their beloved homes and hometowns, seeking a living in cities and other places. As a result, the doors of many houses are tightly closed, without a sound, as desolate as ancient temples, with spiders weaving their webs, becoming their home!!!

How desolate it has become, my hometown!

The beauty of my hometown makes me even more reluctant to return. Faced with reality, my ideal dreams would shatter like a cup filled with red wine dashed against a rock.

Heart in a Sanatorium 290

— Xi Zhen

White wind, white, cold air currents,

White flowers of anemia.

(The large window of the sanatorium room faces south.

Illness is white, dreams are white, alcohol is white, cotton wool is white, medicine bottles and syringes are white, the young nurse is white...

In the morning, the nurse brought a bouquet of flowers and placed them in a large vase in the center of the table by the bed. The fragrance is suffocating.

What is it?

Italian wild roses, blooming towards the southern sun.

A face flashing with the healthy, blood-red glow of youth.

Images drift away, far away, implying the southern sun of Italy, and the bracing, alcohol-tinged breeze of Cheng Lianer.

The patient holds a legendary heart, eyes closed in peaceful repose.

The sick heart needs white treatment.)

In the morning, the streetcar stops in front of the Hamilton Building, routinely spitting out a batch of people and swallowing another, and then clumsily crawls forward on its scorching journey. Looking at the number B27 marked on the back of the car, I am left in front of the building that holds the central hub of culture and commerce of a part of the metropolis.

Walking inside, then—

The daytime sun disappears, I am lifted to the top floor of the building by the elevator, I write my name in the signing-in book, I enjoy the white-hot light of the underground floor, I type "Dear Sir/Madam," "Your letter has been received," "Presenting the matter of XXXX," on the typewriter, I make red and blue marks in the compilation of numbers "...

At dusk, standing on the bustling street, watching the rotation of the wheels and the changing of traffic lights, my self-awareness is awakened: "Creatures under the collective action of the metropolis are 100% mechanized. People are gears, people are cranks, people are screws."

People living under mechanical construction, their blood is surging, their will is agitated, their hearts are pounding, and their brains are hardening.

But hidden behind all this, isn't it the whip of life? Under the whip of life, countless mechanized hearts have blossomed: flowers are pale white, tubercular, neurasthenic, anemic.

Panting palely.

(Say, is the heart sick? A sick heart needs treatment; but I hate the pretentious white of medicine, and anemic patients hate the bleak white, and even in the sanatorium, I hate the weight of the machine; but I also hate the leisure of recuperation.)

One morning, I suddenly saw the newly rising sun, shocked as if by a miracle: at this moment, the bleak white of medicine also carried a bit of healthy red. The sun is constantly moving and burning. In the unfathomable high temperature, it is constantly moving, living, creating days, weaving history. What does mechanical life matter? The machine is moving, running, rubbing, connecting, and thus generates heat and the force of work. Isn't this the best treatment for neurasthenia?

Thinking of the people in the city who are completing the task of another part in the machine, and who have a sick heart, I think of a rusty machine, a machine that is sick: every part is stagnant. There is fuel and there is power, but there is a lack of someone to start it; but in mankind, the one who starts it is the people who are making another part themselves.

If it is said that an unhealthy person should have some exercise, then why let a sick heart remain still? The leisurely treatment in the sanatorium is fundamentally morbid and pale. The symbol of health should be a full, blood-red color.

(It seems that I threw a fire at the sick heart without much thought, and the leisurely, morbid, and medical paleness of the sanatorium disappeared from my eyes.)

A sick heart needs treatment; but this treatment is new and reasonable.

Youth and Cultivation 291

— Hong Ben

Based on my speculation, and confirmed by several senior elders, the youth of twenty or thirty years ago were all "mature beyond their years" and "had a majestic demeanor." This was a reflection of the times and society. The social form of China twenty or thirty years ago was bound to produce such youth. But times have evolved, and now it's completely the opposite. Young people are mostly impetuous and shallow, regarding cultivation as pedantic and rejecting it out of hand. Naturally, this is also a reflection of the times and society. But what if a child who hasn't learned to walk tries to run? Wouldn't they fall?

As a result, many people look down on young people and regret their immaturity. But everyone has this expectation: youth has great hope, and youth has even greater responsibility. The future of the country and society depends entirely on the youth. Today's youth will be the masters of society and the country.

However, it's very dangerous! But I don't despise youth at all. I am one of them.

I just feel an urgent danger for myself. We really need some cultivation.

Before talking about cultivation, it's necessary to make a general point about the common shortcomings of modern youth. In my opinion, the shortcomings of modern youth are not in courage, but in timidity; not in aging, but in impetuosity; not in shirking responsibility, but in lack of perseverance; not in shallow knowledge, but in lack of confidence in seeking knowledge; not in indulging in bad habits, but in lack of genuine hobbies. As a result, everyone naturally walks toward a downward path, unable to extricate themselves. In short, the problem with today's youth is timidity, inertia, lack of ambition, perfunctoriness, shortsightedness, and muddling through. This is their attitude toward themselves, others, and society. As a result, they can't withstand the storms and soon wither. No one has great hope.

I deeply feel that we young people should have the following kinds of cultivation:

First, wash away the heart of inertia and replace it with a spirit of conscientiousness and responsibility. Broadly speaking, this so-called conscientiousness and responsibility means being conscientious and responsible for one's own life.

Second, wash away the timid and conservative mentality and replace it with a spirit of adventure and fortitude. Many great people and great achievements are accomplished in this way.

Third, get rid of the "shirking" mentality and replace it with a spirit of seeking advancement. We young people haven't actually learned much or understand much, but everyone has a bit of complacency. We must know that like the vast ocean of knowledge, we must explore it step by step.

Fourth, get rid of bad habits and replace them with genuine hobbies.

That's all I have to say. I'll leave it at that.
