Shen Bao Local Supplement Movie Special

The Howl of Johnny Weissmuller, Star of "Tarzan the Ape Man" 292

— A Bai

Since the roaring success of "Tarzan the Ape Man" in China, people have been wondering whether Johnny Weissmuller, specially created by God, really has such a strong physique, tree-climbing agility, and beast-catching skills, or whether it's all due to the magic of the camera. Among young people who admire him and women who secretly admire and worship masculine "health" and "strength," it is indeed a frequently and hotly debated topic.

Another thing that audiences around the world have been questioning is his earth-shattering howl. We should remember that in "Tarzan the Ape Man," the world swimming champion didn't speak, except for so-called ape language, elephant language, and other animal languages that we can't understand, and the words "I," "love," and "you" that his white partner Joan taught him. All that was transmitted from the sound system behind the screen to the audience's ears was his loud, long, and modulated howl. The shrillness of the howl made it almost unimaginable that it was a human calling!

In the weeks after the completion of "Tarzan the Ape Man," invitations from people eager to see his true face flooded in. Weissmuller, having been deprived of the taste of socializing for so long, was becoming restless. So he decided to keep the long, shaggy hair of a savage that MGM was eager to use for "Tarzan and His Mate" and strictly forbade him to shave, put on the evening dress that had long bound his burly frame, and went to the party.

As he steadily walked into the middle of the guests, his head and shoulders, supported by his six-foot-three-inch frame, towered above all the men and women in the room. Enthusiastic applause came from the soft hands of the women, and curious gazes were directed at this bull-like figure from the eyes of the men.

Later, a wealthy widow grabbed Weissmuller and walked him to the balcony. He, who was used to quietness, was feeling suffocated by the crowds and felt the need to breathe fresh air, so he happily followed. But the wealthy widow led him all the way to the garden, where she suddenly begged him, "Tarzan, please give me a howl!"

There are more than just thousands of people who are as suspicious and curious as the wealthy widow. Weissmuller has performed publicly at the request of audiences. When more than 6,000 young people gathered at the Shrine Auditorium in Los Angeles for "Youth Week," "Weissmuller stood on the world's largest stage, hesitated for a moment, and took a deep breath, expanding his chest, which was 43 and three-quarters inches wide. The cry was suddenly released from his mouth and spread to every corner of this unique venue.

It has been two and a half years since Weissmuller filmed "Tarzan the Ape Man." For these full eight hundred days, he has been playing the role of "Tarzan and His Mate" under MGM's plan. According to newspaper reports, this film, which is more exciting than "Tarzan the Ape Man," was officially completed in the United States on April 20. And people in the film industry are also rumored that the film has been approved for release by the central authorities. The days when we will see him fighting ferocious beasts and hear his long howls on the screens of this city are not far off!

Film Review

Review of "The Thin Man" 293

— Ling He

The Thin Man 丨Nanjing

Usual detective films are all about creating tension and excitement, making people eagerly wait for the truth to emerge in a bizarre murder case. In other words, it is the greatest responsibility of screenwriters to construct a story that is as tortuous as possible, and of directors to create an atmosphere that is very serious and terrifying. However, not every detective film can achieve this level. On the contrary, they are usually extraordinarily dull, which is not very appealing to "entertainment-seeking" audiences. What they want is to be "delighted" and "slowly sink into the sofa," but the result is a sleepy slumber that is not at all exciting. If they can't even do that, what else can they do? As for our demand that detective films at least have new content, that is even more difficult to obtain in American films at this stage.

As mentioned above, it is indeed true that detective films are not welcomed by the general audience. Therefore, clever filmmakers have had to find other ways. Although they cannot obtain new content, they must at least try new things in form. This is something that we can find considerable proof of in W. S. Van Dyke's "The Thin Man."

We will not ignore the fact that this detective film, like many similar works, has no new content at all. An electrical scholar loses 100,000 shares, and soon after, he disappears. Then, two people die tragically one after another, and another person also goes missing. They are all related to the case. Afterward, the case is solved through the investigation of a retired detective. It turns out that the filmmaker was assassinated and hidden by his legal advisor, and the other two victims were also killed by him because he had received half of the 100,000 shares. In this story, can we find anything better than the so-called lawyer breaking the law? No, like general love or robbery cases, there is nothing worth mentioning.

However, the screenwriter and director have made up for this ordinary content with the form of comedy, so they tried their best to write the detective as a remarkable character. He lives a romantic life, he doesn't care about anything, and at the same time, he is very calm and alert. In his personal life, the description of him and his wife is very interesting and vivid, which breaks up a lot of the dull atmosphere that is common in detective films. Precisely because of this, the director tried his best to portray him, so he became a purely unrealistic and ideal character. The most obvious example is when he and another detective are at Heino's house, he is blowing smoke rings in a tense atmosphere. When he is entertaining the suspects and the perpetrator draws a gun and shoots, he immediately punches him to the ground. Similarly, when he and his wife are joking in bed and a thug breaks in, attempting to commit a crime, he calmly handles the situation and eventually knocks the thug down with his bare hands. This exaggerated portrayal is made even more "miraculous" by William Powell's performance, so the detective's talent makes one dare not believe it.

But does this work end with humor? At least we think the scene where he invites the suspects is still quite dull. Generally speaking, it is better to watch it as a general comedy than as a detective film. Myrna Loy also performed very well.

Zasu Pitts' Ideal Wife 294

— Xin Zhi

Zasu Pitts has been in the film industry for five or six years. She received a lot of honor in "Greed," but she is still single. She not only doesn't have a lover, but she has never even had a partner.

Although her status is far less than that of John Gilbert, the late Rudolph Valentino, and the current Clark Gable and Ramon Novarro, there are quite a few women in Hollywood who admire her, but she doesn't have the slightest attachment to them.

Once, at a tea dance in Hollywood late at night, Zasu Pitts was about to stand up from a secluded seat and go home to sleep when a woman suddenly walked over and sat next to her, greeting her. She opened a bottle of champagne, poured a glass, drank half of it herself, and asked Zasu Pitts to drink the remaining half. She was disgusted, but thinking that she couldn't escape, she had to reluctantly drink it. The woman then further requested her to "open water." Zasu Pitts was in a dilemma, but fearing that she would become angry, she had no choice but to accept her request, while secretly whispering in her ear, "Isn't that your husband over there at the door?" The woman didn't have time to look closely and immediately fled, and Zasu Pitts got a plan to escape.

Zasu Pitts rejected such women more than once, countless times. In social situations, she has never been involved in romance. People in Hollywood regard her character as stupid. But is she really stupid? Doesn't she portray love on the screen with reason and emotion? Originally, she had her reasons.

She hasn't mentioned the issue of marrying a wife yet. She said, "There is no reason not to marry a wife. If I don't marry now, I will marry in the future. It's just a matter of time. But even if I want to have a lover, I will never have one in Hollywood. I think life in the film industry is too dangerous. In the future, I will definitely go to the countryside and become a farmer. I think if I go to the countryside to live, would women in Hollywood be willing to go to the countryside with me?"

So, Zasu Pitts already has an ideal wife in her heart.

Doing Birthday Bad Things, Damned Should Die But Don't Die 295

— Xi Fu

Marie Dressler died. Someone asked why American film magazines didn't have much grand coverage? It seems that even her birthday wasn't advertised as loudly. Of course, grief cannot be expressed in words, only tears and sorrow float on everyone's faces. Indeed, it was a great loss for America and a pain for Hollywood. When her illness became increasingly serious, Hollywood and audiences across the country were praying for her, and President Roosevelt also sent her a telegram, wishing her a speedy recovery. But Heaven didn't pity her, and she passed away. Marie was ill for a total of two years. During that time, she also worked hard for a long time despite her illness. She had always been physically strong, and everyone thought she would recover, but because she took responsibility too seriously, she couldn't take a long-term, complete rest, which led to the fact that the old woman in her sixties couldn't support it anymore. After her death, there was still a film called Living in a Big Way that she wasn't able to start filming, which is especially regrettable.

Furthermore, according to Chinese superstition, especially in the South, it is not good to celebrate birthdays in a big way. Last November 9, Hollywood celebrated the old woman's birthday in a big way. The President also sent a telegram to congratulate her, and the governors of various states in the United States sent her local specialties as gifts. She received no less than hundreds of thousands of congratulatory telegrams. It set an unprecedented precedent in the entertainment world. According to superstitious people, celebrating her birthday did bad things. Then why didn't the damned birthday person die?

Movie novel

Affairs of Cellini (I) 296

— Bi Luo

Starring Constance Bennett and Frederic March, produced by 20th Century Corporation of America

She was born graceful and poised, the Duchess of Medici, so poised and graceful that men who saw her couldn't help but neglect sleep and food. Poised... but also ruthless... Only the Medici family could be so ruthless. But she had been kind once. Once... her eyes lost their shimmering edge, her cherry lips lost their domineering air. Once, her heart became like any woman's heart, easily broken and wounded, as any woman would feel a sudden chill and sigh softly. All morning, he sat high in the council chamber, grandly judging his unfortunate subjects, unfortunate enough to incur his displeasure. All morning, he had been incited by the eloquent Ottaviano, dispatching those criminals as he pleased. This one should die slowly, his flesh cut piece by piece to suffer more; this one should be hanged first, then his body quartered and dismembered; this one should be nailed and slowly burned to death; this one was comparatively fortunate, allowed to be imprisoned in a stone cellar for life, never to see the sun, moon, or stars again. Then Ottaviano mentioned the name of a person awaiting judgment, a man named Benvenuto Cellini, the world's unprecedented goldsmith... artisan. Ottaviano demanded that the Duke sentence him to death. Now the Duchess arrived, also demanding that he be sentenced to death, that audacious madman, daring to lightly disobey her will, failing to present the gold plate she had commissioned by the deadline, simply a contempt for the Medici family's dignity. Ottaviano, hearing that the Duchess also wanted him executed, secretly rejoiced. He bowed to the Duke and said, "This matter is best left to me. This murderer must not be allowed to roam free any longer." The Duchess glanced at the Duke and said, "A murderer! Shouldn't a murderer be hanged?" The Duke shifted uneasily on his throne, unable to withstand his wife's fierce glare. He stammered, "We're just waiting for him to finish those plates. Besides, it was just a bit of swordplay, a bit of trouble, just the kind of thing warriors like." The Duchess's blue eyes flashed with fire, she said impatiently, "Can't we find a second goldsmith in all of Florence?" The Duke smiled ingratiatingly, "Of course, there's no shortage of artisans, but we can't find a second with his genius." Ottaviano, seeing that the Duke had some intention of protecting Cellini, quickly interjected, "There are others accusing him. Even now, there is a plaintiff waiting to request your judgment." As he spoke, with a triumphant smirk, he turned to look at the person who had just been brought in. The Duchess's beautiful eyes were fixed on a girl standing behind that man. She thought to herself that she used to be like that... like peach blossoms in the March spring breeze, clinging to her cheeks, and like dewdrops on a summer morning, lingering in her pupils, but her whole body was flawless and untouched by the world. The man bowed deeply to the Duke's throne and said: (This girl is the youngest daughter of a noble family of Wanqi, this affair is also a great humiliation, a great insult to the royal family...) (To be continued)
